when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她做了一些 , 但事實上 , 是要說未來將會比這個還要多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙來了 , 在1936年 , 在1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴比斯的機器是完全機械化的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這些人都來自數學的觀點 , 但要告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基金會推下電腦科學的數學基礎 , 說: 「 不管你如何製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦的機械機械性 , 像是babbage的 , 或電子 , 像是現今的電腦 , 或未來 , 細胞 , 或再一次 , 機械 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到巴比斯的機器 , 讓它變小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你得到了這個連結 , 在這裡你說這東西的泡沫真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它可以做我們今天用電腦做的事 , 只能慢慢地做 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了給你一個想法 , 它有多慢 , 大概有1/1的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用的卡片 , 被餵食 , 大約有一萬倍的速度降低第一個zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有雷射包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	若你想要做的事 , 你可以加上很多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天 , 這帶給我們什麼樣的 ?
so there are plans .	這裡有計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館逮捕了 , 有數百個計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴布寫著這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組是我們稱之為28計劃的計劃 , 這也是我剛開始的慈善名字 , 他是科學博物館的曲線 , 同時 , 驅使這個計畫建立了不同的引擎 , 我們的計畫是建立它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南韓 , 我們會建立分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	專案有數個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是巴比斯的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 , 第二個是研究這些計畫的研究 , 來決定要做什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三個部分是電腦模擬這台機器的模擬 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它建構時 , 你終於能了解電腦如何運作 , 因為與其在你面前有一小晶片 , 你必須檢視這個謙遜的東西 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我會聽到它運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝爾寫了自己 , 他說 , 當分析引擎存在時 , 它一定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造出來 , 因為他總是用新計劃來飛行 , 但當它在1940年代建立時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我會給你們一些小小的味道 , 用影片的動作 , 顯示cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組的表面 , 它會加上 。 這是在行動中增加的機制 , 所以你想像這台巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們會得到它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像的演說中 , yan藝術hubertorand展示了他的三項計畫 , 在人類和棲息地的照片中 , 拍攝地球的《全球》 , 來自全球各地的個人訪問 , 《網路計劃》中 , 《六十億人》 , 以及他很快的《家》 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、未來、人性、媒體、攝影、攝影 , 包括藝術、氣候變遷、環境、環境、未來、人性、媒體、媒體、媒體、照片
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yan藝術創作者捕捉了脆弱的地球 , 在廣大的角度上捕捉了脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 以飛機來旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我僱用了 , 在大氣中 , 九噸的二氧化碳 ; 這是兩個大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態學 , 一年內 , 我把二氧化碳當成法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以我要怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式做我的碳 , 就像我每次都做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看我去年所做的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯塔沙沙沙 , 很多污染 。

but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年都使用石油比我們發現的還要多三倍 。

our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不穩定 。

we are endangering ourselves .	我們在終結自己 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的接觸演講中 , 理查•雷尼克展示了如何便宜且快速的基因序列是將健康照護轉移到下面 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物技術、健康照護、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷尼克:歡迎來到基因革命的革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向各位展示了人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體是左上方的 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下面是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體 , 男人有x , 當然 , 那個小小的複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是個小小小的小東西讓你不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你當然看到的 , 就是這個二氧化碳結構 , 生物化學字母的密碼 , 或我們稱之為基礎:a、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	在人類基因組中有多少人 ? 三十億人 。
is that a big number ?	那是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以在大數字上扔 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我在這個12800年的每一塊像素上放一個鹼基 , 我們需要3千個螢幕 , 來看看基因 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便說一下 , y染色體決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年後 , 大約四十億美金 , 基因組被定序並發表了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本出版了 , 他們一直在努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在一個像這樣的機器上完成 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一塊鹼基的花費很慢 , 就能花費一塊錢 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	嗯 , 我在這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道它 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	我們現在做的是把基因組做五十個複製 , 我們把這些複製成五十巴士讀完 , 然後我們將它們排序 , 大量的平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這帶到軟體上 , 我們將它組合起來 , 告訴你們這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給大家一張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gigabes , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一個機器之一:一週內有200個gigabes 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變600年 , 沒有這種速度緩慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基礎的價格 , 以定序一個基礎 , 已經下降了一億次 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等於你在1998年把你的汽車裝滿了氣體 , 等到2011年 , 等到2011年 , 你可以開車到木星 , 兩倍 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口 , 價格 , 所有醫學文獻、摩爾法律、舊的定律 , 這是所有新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個邏輯尺寸 ; 你通常會看到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 今年 , 人類基因組的能力是五萬到十萬人的基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們也知道這些基於被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這期待要兩倍、三倍、三倍、三倍或三倍的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室尤其代表了20%的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做 「 北京基因組組織 」 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對贏得這場新月球 , 順便一提 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她展示了舞台2的雌激素接受乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她在治療手術、化療和輻射 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她回來了三階段三度卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	她三年後回來了42歲 , 用更多的卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又回來了阿姆斯托爾•萊姆尼亞 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她接到呼吸失敗 , 八天後就死了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士被治療的方式 , 在十年內 , 會看起來像血液 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	是因為像我同事rickwilson , 在華盛頓大學的基因學院 , 他們決定去看這位女子後期的事件 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他定序了 , 他拿著皮膚細胞 , 健康皮膚 , 及癌症骨髓 , 他在幾週內排序了整個基因組 , 沒有大問題 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他把這兩個基因和軟體相比 , 他發現 , 其它東西中 , 一個部落 , 一兩千個鹼基 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	若你在這個基因中有這種細微的突變 , 你就有90%的可能性能在你生命中得到癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這不幫助這位女子 , 但如果你願意 , 更加嚴重 , 更深刻的影響了她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果有相同的突變 , 它們會得到基因測試 , 然後他們了解它 , 那麼他們就能得到一般的螢幕 , 牠們可以捕捉癌症 , 甚至可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我介紹一下beery雙胞胎 , 診斷出兩個年齡的胚胎 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	她們的媽媽是非常勇敢的女人 , 不相信症狀不會上升 , 透過一些英雄的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學社群 , 事實上 , 他們有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的 , 是兩者的動態症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們被給了 , 他們的症狀已經改善了 , 但他們沒有完全模糊的 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果發現 , 這張圖中有一位叫joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運成為一個叫做生命技術的小組 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是這兩個公司之一 , 讓這些大型基因組定序工具完成 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他做的是 , 他得到了他的孩子的序列 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現的是一系列的突變 , 叫做 「 春天 」 的基因 , 負責在其它東西中產生血清素 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在盧比亞頂端 , 他們給了這些孩子一個半子的先鋒藥 , 他們現在是正常的 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	男士 , 這永遠不會發生任何基因序列 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	在幾年前 , 當時 , 花了十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年 , 一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一百美金之後的一年 , 或花一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動速度的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有個小小的尼克 , 像蝙蝠俠和安靜槍枝 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院的醫院裡 , 像一個家庭受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃飯時 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 把藥送到他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百多次手術 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 拜託我禱告 。 我很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫師在臨床遺傳學中有背景 , 他不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 我們來讓這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 基因中一個單一的突變 , 可以控制程式細胞死亡 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以理論是 , 他有一些免疫的反應 , 基本上是對食物的影響 , 這是一種自然反應 , 造成一些編程的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但 , 規範下面的基因是破壞的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這種資訊 , 包括其他東西 , 當然 , 骨髓移植的治療方式 , 他在底下 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫•米爾•米爾 , 一個新裝置 , 很快地收集生命 , 留下骨頭的痛苦 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中 , 成人的幹細胞可以被用來治療許多條件 , 從帕金森到心臟疾病 。

i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 我們這裡有炸彈 , 他是一位志工捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們將他的標記送到全國各地 , 來拯救一個患有白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	那麼 , 我們要如何收集這塊骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	嗯 , 我們有一個全部的o.r.團隊 , 一般麻醉 , 護士 , 另一位醫生在我身邊 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	炸彈在桌上 , 我們採用這種小針頭 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法基本上是透過軟組織 , 把它放進硬骨頭裡 , 到技術上 , 並且啟發大約十個骨髓 , 每次都有yr.
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠拿到護士 , 把牠放到一個小小 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它拿回我 。 我們再做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	通常大約有200倍 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到了我的手臂結束時 , 我手上有一通電話 , 別說 , 小寶 , 他的尾端看起來更像瑞士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道 , 這個程序在40年內就沒有改變了 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法可以做到 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個最小的侵略方式 , 一個我們稱之為 「 火星礦工 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	火星礦工 , 它的運作方式是在這裡的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們進入了一遍 , 進入髖骨的前方 , 或髖部的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個很有彈性的洞穴 , 有一個特殊的電路器 , 它會留在火星內部 , 沿著海嘯的背景 , 當它移動時 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你很快速地激勵你 , 或出口 , 富人的骨髓很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以透過相同的句子來做多個傳遞 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃可以得到一個特徵 , 當地的麻醉 , 做這種收穫 , 做成一個不安 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	於是我做了一些原型 , 我在史丹佛的小小小的格子 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後 , 我們有兩個大型動物 , 和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 對於我們的驚訝 , 我們不只把骨髓拿出來 , 但我們收到一百倍的幹細胞活動 , 比起正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年就在fda申請了 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是活的病患 , 你可以看到它跟著有彈性的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 會有兩條路 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	在當地的麻醉下 , 做得很遠 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們再次接到 , 大約有三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人的標準方法還要多 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要關心 ? 骨髓是非常富有的成年幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很棒的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體中 , 包括我們骨髓內的血液幹細胞 , 我們已經使用了一系列的幹細胞 , 已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	過去十年間 , 骨髓幹細胞的爆炸 , 來治療病人的其他疾病 , 例如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經系統中治療帕金森和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出去 , 我們是商業化的 , 今年 , 2.2.0人 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望是 , 這會變得更有幹細胞 , 轉換成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人來簽署潛在生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你可以把你自己最小的幹細胞銀行 , 當你年輕的時候 , 在未來 , 用在你需要的未來 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 我們的骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 每年都聚集在史丹佛的社區 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和外科醫師 , 展示了一場爭議的宇宙 , 或許可能回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有 , 它是最漂亮的八維粒子和強迫你所見的 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他的理論中 , garretlitsi的理論上 , 每件事都在他的理論上 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 鴨子 , 檢查那些殺人方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的十八分鐘 , 我要做最好的我可以描述粒子物理學的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常漂亮且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一根珊瑚頭包含了數千個個體 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物持續在突破和分散到遺傳的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨出一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他是怎麼在這個特定的地點 , 比他鄰居的機會 , 或 「 命運 」 或 「 命運 」 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	現在 , 我們要把溫度太高 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以很有意義 , 你知道的 , 我很害怕證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這會持續 , 告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯地對他有相同的複製 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在所有其他的地點中 , 但將它們分離為個人 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分類成了不同的複製 , 是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	與我們不同 , 一個聰明的智商珊瑚會很獨特地準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們我們的現實 , 不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說很奇怪 , 因為我們只有經驗到一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪是首次描述 「 艾丁格斯•奧德斯和他的貓 」 。
the cat likes this version better .	像這種版本比較好 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , chringinger在一個放射性樣本中 , 由量子力學的法則 , 排列成一個國家 , 不被放射線的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這些樣本放射線的範圍中 , 它會發出一種觸發 , 釋放毒物和chringer是死的 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在另一種現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些現實都被每個人分開了 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	儘管如此 , 另一種也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人只經歷一個個體存在 , 而我們沒有看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就像我們每一個人一樣 , 像chrdorder , 是一種珊瑚在不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這個世界如何在微小的規模下運作 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可能在單一句話中總結:所有能發生的一切 , 都能發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切都發生了 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理是關於描述如何發生什麼事 , 以及什麼都不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們 , 每件事都下降到幾何和元素的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	如果這些互動是完美的平衡 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在 , 我來描述我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是如何運作的 , 以及平衡如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一個質子和抗素會加速到光速的速度 , 聚集在碰撞中 , 產生一種純能量的負擔 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量立即將將轉換成一個解剖粒子 , 用偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 在基因va的cer對撞機有17英里的情況 , 當它運作時 , 畫了五倍的電力 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法準確地預測粒子在任何一個碰撞中會產生什麼樣子 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都知道 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理會告訴我們 , 粒子會產生什麼樣的 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須要有大量的質量和能量 , 被質子和抗素帶進來 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子比這種能量限制更大 , 都不會產生 , 且對我們來說仍然是隱形的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新的粒子加速器非常令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會將能量極限於之前所做過的7次數 , 所以我們就得很快地看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	這裡有一系列的解剖粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大多數人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這間房間裡有許多人會幫他們推動 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中立的夥伴 , 叫做 「 中子 」 , 沒有電荷和一個非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相反地 , 上層的平方有非常大的質量 , 將三分之一的質子和中子結合在一起 , 讓原子內部的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左邊和右撇子的種類中 , 也有反對的夥伴 , 帶有相反的載荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉 , 第三代 , 和第一代的載荷相同 , 但有較高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和不同的粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力的作用和電電動電極互動 , 稱為 「 光子粒子 」 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一個非常弱的力量 , 叫做 「 不可想像力 」 , 弱力 , 只與左撇子的物質互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	堅強的力量在一個不同的載荷之間 , 叫做顏色查理 , 來到三種不同的種類:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以稱之為murraygellmann , 為這些名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 有著重力的力量 , 和其質量和旋轉的物質互動 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是要了解的是 , 各式各式各樣的載荷和所有這些力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量與物質相互作用 , 根據每一粒粒子都有的反應 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	目前尚未見過的粒子 , 但是我們確信希格斯粒子 , 是其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子碰撞的主要目的是看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最棒的謎團是我們所看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要向各位展示一個美麗的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用各種不同的粒子數來計算這些不同的粒子 , 就會有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這是很多粒子持續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	這似乎很奇怪 , 大自然有這麼多元的粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們把它們放到他們的載荷上 , 有些美麗的圖案出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 一個負面的電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個平方和下方方方時 , 會產生一個質子 , 它的電量加上一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 它有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩個載荷的結合:超音能和弱點 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超級手段和弱的載荷把粒子在這個兩維空間中 , 電荷荷就是這些粒子和垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會與物質互動 , 相互作用 , 根據它們的掌控和弱點 , 讓這個模式產生 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 聯合國電擊模型 」 , 它在1967年被放回來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大多數人只熟悉電荷 , 不是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯 , 有一個大量的質量 , 打破這個電擊模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會讓弱力非常弱 , 藉由給予極大的粒子 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯坐著這張地平線 , 電磁晶體的光子 , 永續的質量 , 和電荷和電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被這兩度空間的粒子載荷描述出來 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能把強力推出它的兩個載荷方向 , 把力量粒子和這些方向的位置推出 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知的粒子都可以在四維的載荷空間中拍攝 , 把它們放到兩個維度 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子互動時 , 大自然會以完美的平衡為平衡 , 整合四個載荷方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和一個反粒子碰撞 , 它會產生能量 , 和每四個載荷的載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都能產生同一個能量和維持一個零的載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中創造出來 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 載荷一定總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以將電子和中子延伸到一個中子 , 這三種仍然加上0的載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式不僅僅是相當的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 有什麼互動會發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以把這四維空間旋轉 , 讓一個更好的看待強大的互動 , 有一個好對稱的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強烈的互動中 , 一個強強的力量粒子 , 例如 , 與顏色的平面互動 , 例如這個綠色的綠色 , 用不同的顏色來配合這個紅色的標準 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強大的互動每秒都發生了數百萬次 , 在我們的身體的每一個原子 , 把原子核組合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷與三種力量相對 , 不是故事結束的終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能包含兩種慈善機構對重力的反應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們包含這些 , 每一粒粒子都有兩種不同的旋律 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開 , 在六維的載荷空間中提供一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這種模式可以配合我們目前最好的知識 , 大自然是如何在這些元素粒子中建造出來的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在我們能和實驗的極限上 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小的尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙的運作方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但我現在要討論一些新的和古老的想法 , 關於我們尚未知的事物 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們是否能在整個基礎上取得我們的手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有粒子和力量 , 讓宇宙完全相似 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測我們會看到的新粒子 , 何時會達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理上有一個古老的概念 , 這種所謂的載荷模式 , 不是非常對稱的 , 可以從一個更完美的模式來突破希格斯粒子如何突破電子圖案 , 來給電磁晶體 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了要做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新的載荷方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新方向時 , 我們就會猜測粒子在這個方向有何作用 , 然後我們就可以把它和其他人一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們很明顯地猜想 , 我們就能在六度載荷的標準載荷中建構成這種完美模式的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 這種特定的選擇對應了孫子的理論引進了pati和alam的理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的單位模式時 , 我們可以看到幾種不同的差異 , 粒子似乎是錯的 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是單位化的理論 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋求更大、更對稱的模式 , 包含了組織的模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種獨立的模型預測了這兩種新的力量粒子的存在 , 這應該是像弱力一樣的 , 只有弱勢者 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	我們現在可以在七度空間中旋轉這一組載荷 , 來考慮關於物質粒子的真相:第二代和第三代物質在六維載荷的空間中有相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不獨特地辨識出他們的六個載荷 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在一個標準載荷空間上 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間工作 , 那麼我們就能把獨特的新載荷放在每個粒子上 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度內旋轉 , 看看整個模式看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡 , 我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質的世代 , 由一個稱之為 「 三性 」 的對稱 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	8維度的這個特定模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最多例外的謊言團體的模式 ,  e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這種謊言團體是平滑的 , 用248度形狀的形狀 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個模式的每個角度對這個複雜和美麗的形狀的對稱 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦的曲線 , 相對論 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	由量子力學組成 , 這種形狀的幾何數 , 可以描述宇宙在最小的規模中如何運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀在八維空間中活著的形狀是非常漂亮的 , 它會讓數千個可能的粒子之間的互動 , 每一面都是這種複雜的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	隨著我們旋轉 , 我們可以看到許多其他複雜的模式在這個領域中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	藉由特定的旋轉 , 我們可以透過這八度的對稱軸 , 看所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 就像任何單位一樣 , 我們可以看到一些新的粒子被這個模式所需要的洞 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	這裡有20個差距 , 新的粒子應該是 , 其中有兩種是由patalam粒子所填補的 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置 , 我們知道這些新的粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的規模 , 但有顏色查理和強力的互動 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	把這些新粒子填滿了這個模式 , 給予我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8模式非常深刻的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的觀點 , 這種偉大的數學美麗 , 可以描述粒子互動的真相 , 以最小的想像力來描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	這個想法 , 大自然被數學所描述的不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的偉大書 , 不斷地打開我們的聚會 , 寫在數學語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓圈和其他幾何的數字 , 沒有人可以理解單一詞 ; 沒有這些 , 一個人在黑暗的實驗室中圍繞著 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導來描述粒子物理學的數學 , 只用三角形 , 圓形和其他幾何數字 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這些東西時 , 數學可以組合黑暗的實驗室 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但在這個數學的核心是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這個數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 作為一個成長的珊瑚 , 粒子在所有可能的地點上互動 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著越來越多的圖案出現在使用新機器 , 像是大型的強子撞撞機 , 我們可能能看到大自然是否用這種模式或不同的形式 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這種發現的過程是很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc發現了這8個圖案的粒子 , 那就很酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現了新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但對e8理論來說很糟 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說 , 對我來說很糟 。
now how bad would that be ?	那有多糟糕 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其他的理論很長 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	其中有許多困難的工作 , 知道大部分這些點子可能不會發生在大自然中 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這正是理論物理的樣子:有大量的維度 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	儘管有任何大型投資 , 可能是情緒上升的 , 當它沒有成功時 , 可能很難放棄一個研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學中 , 如果某樣東西沒用 , 你就得要把它弄出來 , 嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一能維持衛生和達成幸福的方式就是維持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我試過我能生活最好的平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生命 , 同樣在物理、愛和衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向之間的平衡 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我從事的物理學 , 我仍然知道我活在一個好生活中 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十多年來 , 我住在馬多島 , 一個非常漂亮的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在是宇宙中最棒的謎團之一 , 讓我的父母如何在生存時間中 , 不用完全組成全職員 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓你們在那個秘密上 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我家的辦公室 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能注意到這些美麗的觀點是相似的 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心租金讓我花時間去做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	活著的存在很艱難 , 但它讓我活在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 在我的生活中 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	讓我花了很多時間和超級智慧的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級智慧的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能了解了百分之二 , 但我仍然很愛它 。 所以我要聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的理論是:我習慣珊瑚礁 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:那是對的 , 最少人的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 重力和量子理論聚在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以你說 , 我們應該考慮宇宙 , 在它的心中 , 最小的事物 , 不知何謂 「 可能性 」 是嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的規模中 , 是否有規模 , 還是嗎 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:嗯 , 現在我向各位展示的圖案 , 對於我們所知的元素粒子物理學的了解 , 已經對一個非常美麗的形狀做出反應 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這是我所說的 , 我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有著很驚人的相似性 , 並且它能符合這個e8的圖形 , 可能是其他的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我為你們展示的這些觀點圖案 , 代表這個高度敏感的物體的對稱性 , 會在我們體驗的空間中移動和舞蹈 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這會是解釋我們所看到的所有元素粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 解釋電子 , 以較小的弦振動 , 我知道你不喜歡把理論震動在裡面 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何把電子視為e8 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱性之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 隨著時間的形狀移動 , 它是扭曲的 。 而它的方向在移動時 , 它的方向是我們所看到的粒子 。 所以它會是克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 電子是怎麼關係的 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	更大嗎 ? 更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:正如我們所知的電子是關鍵的粒子 , 所以這會在最小的規模下降到最小的規模 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論上解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都在擴張和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我會用珊瑚類比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	以這種方式來說 , e8的進步的方式是 , 它的形狀是每一時間在太空中加入的 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀的扭曲方式 , 形狀的形狀是扭轉這個曲線的表面 , 就是原始粒子本身的樣子 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子領域理論 , 他們會把自己當作點 , 以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我是否能讓它更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它是一種奇蹟的感覺 , 我肯定想要了解更多這個 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來了 。 這絕對令人驚嘆 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	合法的黑猩猩研究者珍妮亞爾提到塔卡爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 幫助非洲的小鎮居住著威脅的動物 。
