so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 為了讓它成為100歲 , 你不只需要有很好的生命方式 , 你也必須贏得遺傳量 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 能幫助慢、逆轉 , 或甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 有99個東西可以老化我們 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	除掉你的腦袋 , 只需要幾分鐘 , 大腦細胞會死去 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩得太難 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀了你的車子 , 卡車永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以複製 , 我們的大腦可以用平原來槍枝 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	錯了太多事 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 數兆個 「 t 」 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年都將自己轉過來 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉到那裡時 , 就會造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	基本上它建構出來的 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像現在 , 當我們都有了atatbum或agmsalbums , 我們會複製一份複製 , 讓我們的朋友們複製了 「 催化劑 」 , 很快就有成功的世代 , 像垃圾一樣 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的老年人在一個比12歲的小孩的比例快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果你沒有辦法慢慢你的老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡做些什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	重點是 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 對女性來說 , 比較多 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線上 , 我們在桌上留了大約12年 。
these are years that we could get .	多年來 , 我們就能得到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 他們會多年來會免費慢性疾病、心臟病、癌症、糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法是把這些失望的年齡看世界各地的文化 , 人們活到一百歲到十倍的年齡比我們更大 , 壽命壽命的速度是近十多年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍區大約是125英哩 , 來自義大利海岸 , 在薩丁尼亞島 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 而是在高地 , 一個叫做nuoro建議的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡 , 我們有這個區域 , 男人活得最長 , 比我們在美國還多的10倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只接觸到一百歲 , 他們就這樣做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 十二歲的居住地仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 喝木頭 , 可能比他們更年輕60歲 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實是回到基督徒的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	實際上是一片布朗的文化被隔離了 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這塊土地非常不穩定 , 大部份都是牧羊 , 一般的生態活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食大部分是以植物為基礎的 , 用他們能帶到田地上 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一大堆無線電的麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂 , 由荷蘭的動物組成 , 一類的起士 , 如此一來 , 蜜蜂的酸度高 , 而不是從玉米脂的動物身上 , 還有一種種類型的葡萄糖 , 比世界上任何所謂的酒精還要高 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密我認為 , 他們更能組織他們的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最可觀的元素之一是他們如何治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你曾經注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時暫停 。
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 老年人就會得到你有的平等 , 你的智慧越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你去了薩丁尼亞州的酒吧 , 而不是去看運動節目的瑞典日曆 , 你會看到一個月經的中央人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 不只對你老年老的父母要把他們關在家裡 , 大約有四到六年的壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子來說 , 他們有較低的死亡率和較低的疾病率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊找到了第二個藍色區 , 大約800英里的東南部 , 在奈及利亞南部 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okowa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的基礎 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群被發現的 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方 , 人們擁有世界上最長的殘疾壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活了很長一段時間 , 很快就死在他們的睡眠中 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性行為之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們活得比美國平均的平均壽命還要長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍之多 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	十五歲的殖民和乳癌的速度 , 在美國大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的第六度 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化已經證明了這些數字 , 他們有強烈的教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們怎麼辦 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物的飲食 , 充滿了蔬菜 , 裡面有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍的湯瑪 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的食物更重要 , 就是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略 , 可以保持過度 , 如你所知 , 在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們從小盤子中吃掉 , 所以他們通常會在每一塊地吃少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其是服務家人風格 , 你可以無意地吃東西 , 當你在說話時 , 他們會在櫃子裡吃食物 , 然後把食物帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的廣告 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混亂所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食是撒哈拉 , 帽子 , 吃飯 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人會說 , 在他們的餐之前 , 要提醒他們 , 當他們胃痛時 , 不再吃百分之八十 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它需要一半小時的感覺 , 才能從你的貝兒到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要阻止80%的情況 , 它幫助你保持那件事情 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞一樣 , okowa有幾個社會建設 , 我們能和長壽聯繫在一起 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道 , 孤立殺死了 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國平均有三位好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在下降到一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運地出生在okinawa , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你自動有一半的朋友 , 和你經歷過生命的人 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 馬拉i 」 , 如果你遇到幸運的話 , 你就想分享這個責任 , 如果你遇到壞事 , 孩子會生病 , 你總是有你背後的人 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特殊的摩亞 , 這五位女士已經結合了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常 , 在美國 , 我們將成人的人生分成兩個部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們有工作的生命 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 這意味著退休到簡單的椅子 , 或往亞利桑那州去玩高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在奈及利亞語言中 , 甚至沒有退休的詞 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	相反地 , 有一個字會讓你整生的生命 , 這個字是 「 伊基加西 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約是翻譯 , 意思是 「 你早上醒來的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	在這個十二歲的凱特•馬斯特 , 他的ikigai正帶著這個火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對於這一百歲的漁夫來說 , 它持續捕魚 , 每週三次捕魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 國家老化的機構 , 給了我們一個問題 , 給予這些中央人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們是非常文化的直覺 , 那些提出問題的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上知道為什麼他們早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	在這102歲的老婦女 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾曾曾祖父 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101年分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 我問她 , 要抱著一個偉大的學位 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放回來 , 她說: 「 感覺就像跳躍到天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個很棒的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理學的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區塊 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	一陣子 , 我們看著明尼蘇達的禱告 , 實際上 , 有一個非常高的中亞人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但這是因為所有年輕人離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口 , 在七天的冒險家集中 , 加州的羅馬林德達州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	專家是保守的金屬師 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們在星期五的星期五的日日日日日日日日日慶祝他們的日子 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個《24小時聖誕節》 , 他們稱之為 「 。 」
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們不尋常的長壽 , 相較於說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一位先進主義的女人 , 他們的壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差別在男性中 , 甚至更為宣佈 , 他們預期要活大約十一年 , 比美國的郡還要長11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這是一項研究 , 追蹤了大約有七萬人的研究 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史蒂夫研究 , 我認為它最終可以說明這個藍色區域的前景 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個很大的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白色、黑人、猶太人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共同點是一組非常小的生命型態 , 牠們對大部分的生命都很小的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	慷慨: 「 章魚 」 、 「 第29 」 』 , 上帝談到樂高和種子 , 關於綠色植物 , 可能錯過的就是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在非常嚴肅的情況下採用這個聖誕節 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們有多忙 , 他們有多壓力 , 孩子們需要開車 , 他們停止一切 , 關注上帝、社交網路 , 接著 , 在宗教中 , 都是大自然行走 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種權力不是偶爾發生的 , 權力是每週 , 每週都在做 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有它很困難 , 沒有錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	進步主義者也傾向於與其他偉大主義者聚在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一位先進主義派對 , 你看不見人們在打擊吉姆•貝姆 , 或推動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談論他們的下一大自然走路 , 擴張相反 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會影響彼此 , 以深刻且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 有著威廉的伊斯蘭•哈雷姆 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	wharehareham97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是數百萬美金 , 但當一個競爭者想要6 , 000美金來建立隱私的本質 , 他說: 「 為了我自己做這件事 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 接下來三天他出去買水泥 , 並且在周圍騷擾游泳 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的 , 也許在第四天 , 他終於在手術室裡 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌上的人 ; 那個人在做開放的手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97年 , 他每個月仍然在做20個開放手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	愛德華 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末 , 他喜歡放上板子 , 丟下roosososter的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這兩座城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從她的日子開始 , 讓她的重量很高 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她在她的根廷有色彩1994年的科迪爾維爾維爾 , 把聖貝納納米羅的自由公路撕下來 , 她仍然有七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在19個硬幣前進 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是你遇過的唯一一個人 , 他的腳踏車在撒哈拉沙漠的沙漠中 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險比起火星的撞擊 , 更加駭人 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 。 」 她對我說: 「 一個陌生人 ,
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 在這個三種文化中 , 常見的決定者是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地把它放到九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們從此開始進行了兩項藍色區塊 , 而這些共同的決策者確保了事實 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要在這裡做個實驗 , 沒有運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了他們的生命 , 讓他們不斷被困在實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這一百歲的奈瓦婦女在地面上升下 , 他們坐在地板上 , 每天30到40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行到商店 , 或教堂或朋友的房子會發生一個行走 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何良心 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做yard工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想把蛋糕混合起來 , 它們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	這樣燃燒的卡路里和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做意外的實體活動時 , 是他們享受的事物 。 他們傾向走路 , 唯一能證明認知衰退的方式 , 他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式建立他們的生活 , 讓他們有正確的外表 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每個文化都需要時間轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁裔人禱告 , 第七天的演員禱告 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這個祖先的角落 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你陷入傷害或壓力後 , 會引發一種稱為 「 內流素反應 」 的現象 , 和阿茲海默症的所有東西有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	每一天你慢下來15分鐘 , 你就會轉變成一種更反射的反射性狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有義大利的目的感 , 愛基加西 , 例如奇蹟 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的 , 他們在他們的人生中活著 , 值得有七年的壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一點 , 不太難賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 但很多豆子和子孫 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	牠們有策略 , 持續過度 , 把它們從平板上消失 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	而這一切的基礎是他們如何連結的 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們首先把他們的家人 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於屬於信仰基礎的社群 , 這值得四到十四、14年的壽命 , 如果你每個月做這四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們是否會出生 , 或對人有自動地圍繞著自己和右派人 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從脆弱的研究中知道 , 如果你的三位最好的朋友是肥胖的50% , 你將會有過重的機會 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 那會對時間的影響很大 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友的回收概念是實體的活動 , 繁榮 , 或玩香菸 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點 , 但他們吃得太好了 , 他們會信任和信任 , 這將會對時間有最大影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不會成功 。 世界上的歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	練習計畫通常從一月開始 , 他們通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	長期來看 , 沒有短暫的修復 , 或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想到 , 你的朋友是長期冒險 , 因此 , 可能是你能做最重要的事 , 多年來 , 多年來 , 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨西哥的電力 , 一扇窗戶從明確的轉換到一個開關的角度 ; 一個充滿音樂的水母 , 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡里娜•莫塔說:該是玩它的時候了 。 摩塔會引領我們驚訝和酷的材料 , 並且說 , 我們會想知道我們能做些什麼 , 去做實驗 , 更有趣和有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一位在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父建造了一台車 , 一台洗衣機 , 讓他能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他不能負擔一輛車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有一段時間 , 當我們了解事情如何運作 , 如何做 , 這樣我們就能建立並修復它們 , 或最少的決定要購買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀的第二半期 , 許多的醫生都失敗了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者和公開資源模型將這種知識帶到我們的生活中 , 並且我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 以組成的東西組成 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	最重要的部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統的材料 , 像是紙和紡織物 , 以及它們如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些驚人的、自閉的塑膠 , 會改變形狀 , 繪製電力 , 那些改變顏色的顏色 , 發出的顏色 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以 , 受教育的墨水允許我們繪製電路 , 而不是用傳統的列印電路板或電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我握住的例子中 , 我們用它來創造一種觸覺感測器 , 透過把我的皮膚轉換成這個小燈 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	受教育的墨水被藝術家所使用 , 但最近的發展指出我們很快就能在雷射印刷機和筆記上使用它 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一片加密的綿羊 , 充滿了無色的光能粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 一般的加密單單單只會在邊緣的光線 , 這張圖顯示在整個表面上 , 當我把光線轉向周圍 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	其中有兩個已知的應用 , 包括內部設計和多種觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	溫度的顏色會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱的盤子上 , 只能讓溫度比雄性更高 , 看看會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 其中一個原則的應用是 , 在其他東西中 , 嬰兒瓶裡 , 會指出內容是很酷的飲用品 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是少數人所知的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年來 , 他們會在許多我們每天使用的物品和技術上 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們還可能還沒有飛行車科幻小說 , 但是我們能有牆壁 , 改變顏色的溫度 , 按鍵板 , 讓它變得相反 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 為何我今天要談到智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇的是 , 事情如何運作 , 和它們是怎麼做的 , 但我相信我們應該更了解我們的世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技的組成並不足以組成 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在小的量子中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用到如何使用它們 , 很少是說他們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以現在 , 他們大部分都存在在貿易秘密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業都能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 三年前 , 三十年前 , 我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是我們的網站 , 任何想加入我們、分享實驗、發表資訊 , 鼓勵別人 , 每當他們能做 , 加入資源 , 像是像我們這樣的製造者一樣 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、集體的資料庫 , 可以在智慧材料上產生資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要關心有多聰明的材料 , 以及它們所做的是什麼 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們不能塑造我們不了解的事物 , 而我們不明白和用它來塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品 , 穿著衣服、我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們活在一個聰明的材料中 , 我們應該知道和了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的 , 創新一直都被固定者所燃燒 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 護士 , 不是專家 , 曾經是發明家 , 改善在山上自行車 , 到半行車、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 物質科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	在伊利諾大學 , 兩個科學家明白了這點 , 當他們在一個簡單的方法上發表了一篇文章 , 來製造生產力的墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦布朗•布克 , 他沒有經歷過化學物質 , 直到那時 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者太空中複製了實驗 , 只用無限的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一顆大烤箱 , 他甚至做了他自己的旅館混合物 , 根據另一位科學家/maker的直覺 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦後來在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括他嘗試的所有事情 , 沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	約旦的主要創新是採取一個實驗 , 在大學的一個好的實驗室 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重建它 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿起他剩下的和破壞的過程 , 更簡單的改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想要提到她的專案目標是要強調材料的表現品質 , 同時專注於建造者的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 他們教導我們如何運作 , 但在他們的設計中限制影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , hannah的方法是要建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 讓我們從預防的限制 , 來教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以 , 在漢娜有很多令人印象的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	「 紙子講者 」 , 我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅紙 , 連接到一個mp3的玩家和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的mcelocoho的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙人 , 從簡單的銅板上 , 變成發電製造和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的協議 , 允許任何人複製並複製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學中最可預期的一部分之一 , 它使我們能創造出便宜的電子電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的動脈工作 , 她分享她的發現 , 打開了一系列的新可能性 , 讓這一系列的新可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	創作者有趣的是 , 我們創造出了熱情和好奇心 , 我們不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常從不傳統的角度來解決問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現替代方案或更好的方式來做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人的實驗 , 更多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商們的知識 , 我們得要創造更好的機制 , 真正能服務我們所有人 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得tednelson是1970年代初期 , 他寫道: 「 你一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是那些大型主要的科學家 , 只關心科學家 , 甚至沒有人夢想在家裡 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你一定要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 關於新興科技的先進知識是確保我們未來所說的最佳方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們進入了玻璃泡泡 , 鎖住門 , 壓迫我們 , 仰賴我們的眼睛 , 儘管我們只能在我們面前看到幾輛車 , 但如果車能與彼此分享他們的位置和動力 , 用預測模式來計算所有人的安全路線 ?
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•亨利:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外意外可能會避免能避免能避免能避免有耐心的意外 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們來面對這個問題:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不想思考的一件事 , 但事實上 , 宗教的意圖和好運的查爾斯出現在世界各地的達爾蘭板上 , 我們知道它是真實的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國年齡十六歲到十九歲的死亡原因 , 導致死亡和75%的意外對抗毒品或酒精 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以確定 , 但我記得我第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是一位年輕的駕駛在高速公路上 , 車在我面前 , 我看到的是布拉克的光線 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好 , 沒錯 , 這個傢伙慢下來 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我站在公車上 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這個傢伙不是慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個傢伙停下來 , 停下來 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在巴克上滑雪了 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得ab踢了 , 車子仍然持續下去 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣部落 , 車子被被安裝 , 很幸運地 , 沒有人被傷害 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車停下來 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變開車的經驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們想一下開車的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車 , 閉上門 。 你在玻璃泡泡中 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接理解你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你被指控 , 將它分散在一半的路上 , 在其他金屬巨大的巨人身上 , 在超級human的速度上 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指導你兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 各位的眼睛不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但是人們要求你做類似的事 , 你想做一台車 , 他們要怎麼做 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	用你的眼睛從路上看 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看你在哪裡 , 轉向你的盲目點 , 開車道路 , 不用看你在哪裡去 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人一樣 , 這是最安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做個選擇 , 我會在這裡 , 看吧 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常 , 我們會做一件很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做些什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺出錯或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數意外的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我看不到它 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在存在 , 可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子和彼此交換資料 , 我們將能看到的不只是三輛車 , 三輛車背後 , 到右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們真的能看見車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到我們面前的車子的速度 , 看看那傢伙的速度有多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙走到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算和演算法和預測模式 , 我們將能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 沒有 。 車子 , 不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和動力 。
they travel down roads .	他們走下路 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們都在出版的路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於近期的車子是不是很容易的預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算 , 當你在車裡和一些摩托車員來了 ! 85英里 , 一小時 , 我知道你有這種經驗 , 沒有 「 走出來 」 的經驗 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上可能是上半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、20、30英哩後 , 有人看過那個傢伙 , 只要一輛車 , 把他放到地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 高估他會持續85英里 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車子會在他的耳朵上 , 說: 「 順道一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車 , 看著 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出合理的預測 , 關於車子如何運作 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	那麼 , 我們該怎麼到那裡呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 用汽車之間的位置資料 , 來分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和一台攝影機 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我在哪裡 , 和我有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	透過電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子是哪裡的 , 有點像 , 他們在哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他車一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有精確的點子 , 有點像其他車子的位置 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享這些資料 , 如果他們彼此對話 , 會如何呢 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	波爾伯特和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當難民估計組合時 , 甚至是光線交通 , 汽車共享gpps資料 , 我們將這個研究從電腦模擬和機器人測試的廣告取出了實際的感測器 , 目前在這些機器人上 , 如同creo相機、gps、gps , 以及兩次的雷射器 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也在一個很短的溝通廣播廣播 , 機器人彼此對話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相抵抗時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在將更多的機器人加入混合中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你遇到太多的章節時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先化 , 那就是預測模式幫助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預期的軌跡 , 你不會對那些包裝的注意力不多 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點不錯的傢伙 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他在做這件事 , 你知道如何 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道哪個驅動者 , 要讓任何人走出去 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做才能做到最好的所有人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	怎麼能讓這些車子摔角 , 「 你需要走路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它依賴兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二個是駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 做一些事 , 他們可能不是最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始一系列的研究 , 做司機模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測駕駛是否向前看 , 向下看 , 看著手機 , 或喝咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測出意外 , 我們能預測誰 , 哪個車位是最好的位置 , 去計算所有人的安全路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術已經存在了 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們所面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願能分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常令人沮喪的點子 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談到其他車子 , 我們會在路上走下 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私的方式 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看看你的執照數字 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車能在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們能考慮一下 , 如果你真的不想在你後面的青少年 , 知道你正在打破 , 你要去死的停止 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由分享我們的資料 , 我們能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子來加速你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xpm創辦人彼得.狄納斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金的夢想 , 透過飛到上空的大氣中 , 飛到零的重量 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短暫的演講、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、太空、太空、太空、
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	史蒂芬•霍金的彼得•狄納斯在0ggggg的零箱上 , 彼得.
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	那些知道我有多熱情 , 我是要打開空間前面的 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界上的專家重力 , 重力的體驗是不可思議的 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次遇見他 , 由基因組組組組組成 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們握住的競爭 , 第二個x獎項 , 在10天內 , 將100個人類基因組序列出來 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一種叫做基因組的100個人 , 我們將它定序成一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊特的椅子 , 那個事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了教授霍金 , 他說他的夢想是去旅行空間 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你們到那裡 , 但我可以把你帶到零中 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	然後他說: 「 絕對 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	地球上唯一能體驗零的方法 , 其實是肢體飛行 , 沒有重量飛行的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿一台飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 飛過了25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 重兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你再次做一次 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的重量 , 以致於美國太空總署訓練他們的太空人多久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才能成為營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛到史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機構和一間公司飛機操作者說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了這個人 。
and he wanted to go .	他想去了 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的允許 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在肯尼太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場媒體會議 , 我們宣佈了我們的意願去做一個零和派對 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	若它真的很順利 , 我們可能會做三種悖論 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼他想去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他對我說 , 對我來說 , 非常動 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命是一場災難造成的風險 。
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我想 , 人類的種族沒有未來 , 如果它不會進入太空 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵公共利益 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到kenededy太空中心 , 在美國太空總署車內 , 進入零飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人做捐贈 , 我們收入了150萬美元的捐贈 , 給孩子的慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedtster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個伺服器 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們正在監視他的血液2的二氧化碳 , 他的心率 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們所有東西都在一個緊急情況下設立 ; 上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從垃圾桶降落 , 在那裡 , 梭狀會脫離和土地 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我的夥伴lironlichberg , 我小心地讓他變成0g 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 讓他去體驗無關的重量 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	一開始 , 醫生說了一切都很棒 , 他很笑 , 我們說了吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以 , 我們做了第二個小行星 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的把一個蘋果漂浮在伊斯蘭的牛頓 , 因為哈佛教授們在劍橋上抱著同樣的椅子 , 這位是伊斯蘭的牛頓 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 一個第五和六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	一個第七、八歲 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他很高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶中 , 在我們這顆星球的一生中 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個廣泛的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家davidbolinsk的現場有3分鐘的動畫 , 顯示細胞內的細微生物 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫療、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化、視覺化
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•波里斯基動畫一個細胞動畫一個細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫師 , 我來自一些不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 從我長大 , 真相和美麗的表達 , 在藝術和現實和科學的美麗 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩件事都很美好 , 但他們兩者都有非常美好的事物 , 可以用科學的理想看待 , 數學幾乎就像是科學家想約會的雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是說真相的表達 , 像是很棒的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你能珍惜的東西 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是很強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	他們是獨一無二的 , 有時很有用的 , 通常在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以動一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 通常對不在科學裡的人來說都是相反的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是描述美的方式 , 如果你了解語言和語言的合成 , 通常 , 才會被描述出真實和美麗的主題 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , e=mc正方形 , 如果你看看宇宙的永續發展 , 那裡有一個人類理想的理念 , 你可以看到生命必須從宇宙中演化出來 , 這些都是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我當作醫學插圖師 , 我從我父親教導的動畫和視覺導師 , 我想要找出一個方法來幫助人們了解生物科學 , 透過圖片 , 說故事 , 以說故事 , 讓人們不見得被賦予 , 且可以被教導 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生常常在環境中聚集在環境中 , 他們學到的是有真相和美感的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是比較的 , 它會被吸引到真實和美麗 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞的古老感應湯 , 你把雞放在那裏 , 直到雞的尾巴已經消失了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生做這件事 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我有一間電話 , 來自哈佛的羅伯特•路易斯 , 在分子和細胞生物學系中 , 幾年前 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊有興趣 , 我會真正地改變醫療和科學教育如何在哈佛做 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以 , 我們開始探索細胞 , 來探索分子和細胞內的真相和美麗 , 讓學生能夠了解一個更大的圖片 , 讓他們能在這些事實上都能用 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	細胞的心智影像是很大的 , 很複雜的城市 , 由微型海灘所佔有的 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微生物真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微生物 , 是美國奈米科技學家的靈活性 , 是自我挑選、精確、精確、精確的裝置 , 是由胺基酸所組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微游生物的力量是如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	他們能發揮細胞如何複製 , 力量我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	他們力量了我們的腦袋 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想知道如何把這個故事弄成一個動畫 , 將是哈佛的生物建議中心 , 哈佛的網站 , 哈佛的分子和細胞生物學的學生 , 除了所有細微的資訊 , 以外 , 這些學生會有內在的視覺化 , 以外 , 讓這些學生們能在所有細胞的真相中發現 , 並且在他們的心中確認它們的心中 , 讓它們的心靈感激發 , 能夠被發現 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們藉由觀察這些分子如何組成 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 就是 , 這裡有一座巨噬的大樓 , 牠們正在觸碰捕捉牆的表面 , 它們會從附近的牆上拿起資訊 , 裡面有一種訊息 , 顯示在外面的某些地方 , 無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊 , 使他們停下來 , 使他們內心化 , 使他們能改變他們的形狀 , 並試著從這個捕捉到找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以 , 我們必須和哈佛科學家和資料資料模型合作 , 原本是準確的分子模型 , 找出它們如何移動 , 找出他們做了什麼 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何用一種真理的方式來做這件事 , 來實現發生了什麼事 , 但不太真理 , 細胞裡的配偶會阻止病毒發生的狀況 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是三分鐘的讀者的第一版本 , 是我們所製作的電影的第一面版本 。 這是一項正在進行的計劃 , 接下來四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這條路 , 看看細胞製造這些小步行機器的路徑 , 他們稱之為ksins , 把這些巨大的大型螞蟻挑戰一個對象的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	拜託 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內部的力量非常了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器彼此互相互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們把資訊傳給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	他們會造成不同的事發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造它在果蠅上需要的零件 , 來自來自細胞核能的資訊 , 由這些分子來解讀基因的分子 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡 , 不會有這些小小小的微生物 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器的缺乏之中 , 已經有了不穩定的 , 克里斯 , 非常快 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedex運送細胞的傢伙 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做ksin , 他把一堆全新的製造蛋白質帶到細胞裡 , 不管是它是身處的 , 不管是有機的 , 不管是要建造東西或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	而我們每個人都有大約十萬件東西在你100兆個細胞內 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不管你感覺多懶惰 , 你都沒有真正的做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望你們回家想這點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們在學習細胞機械的一些東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們想出了一切 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道發生了什麼事 , 我們真的能夠掌控我們對我們的健康 , 和未來的世代 , 以及我們要活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這種方法來發現更真實的真理 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但很驚人的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微小的細菌 , 足以察覺到細胞的需求 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 , 讓細胞做該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 協助我們身體的巨大特性 , 他們永遠無法正確地看到功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受節目的其他節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝基•布蘭頓計劃了一年 , 看到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的營地變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她的經歷 , 成為一個無家可歸的美國人 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、幸福、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、故事故事、故事、快樂、生活、生活、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會、社會、社會、社會、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝多•布蘭頓:我是無家可歸的一年 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個好奇的人 , 所以22年來 , 身為記者 , 我學會如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了我如何做的事之一 , 就是成為隱形的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成了一名無家可歸的無家可歸 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我把我的工作當作報紙編輯 , 在我父親在那一年二月的二月後 , 決定要旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我很辛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事時 , 有很多我想要感受和處理的事物 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都停下來了 。 我決定 , 一年內活在一輛車上 , 這樣做就好像一個很長的營地旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓包包起來 , 我的rotweiler和我的營火裝到1975年的飛行車 , 把車退到陽光上 , 完全無法意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平等生活在永久的結構中 , 甚至是陰影 , 有價值 , 身為一個人 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒意識到他人的負面感知 , 可能影響我們的現實 , 如果我們放下它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車上很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地展示了 , 我常常吃 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間重新放鬆和悲傷 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱症 , 我父親的死亡就在此 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我必須得到全職的工作 , 來支付鈔票 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時的春天轉變成一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	任何地方都不可能公園 , 不用很明顯 , 我和一隻貓在一起 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓在車上穿過一扇開窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	蛋白質進入了小白天照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	無論如何 , 我都用辦公室大樓的員工 , 卡車停止 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共餐廳洗澡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度很少降低了80度的水平 , 使得睡眠很難睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中旋轉了 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	在我的冰箱中 , 數小時內 , 冰塊被融化 , 非常糟糕 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我買不起公寓 , 或無法負擔擔不起公寓 , 讓我能有推特和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱能讓我生病到我車外的五十英尺外面的公共餐廳時 , 我用一塊錢和一條垃圾桶當成廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天天天氣設置時 , 溫度降低了 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面臨了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停了一間不同的地方 , 這樣我會避免被警察所注意到 ,
i didn't always succeed .	我不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到我人生的掌控 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它是怎麼發生的 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者來當一個無家可歸的女人 , 活在車上 , 帶著我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商並沒有降低 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華 , 我的理智 , 我的價值觀 , 所有關於我所留下的一切 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入深入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終 , 有人把我推向無家可歸的醫療診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我走了 , 三天沒有洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和任何人一樣很沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是喝酒 , 或高度 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數位無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 。 為什麼你在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人都看不到我是無家可歸的 , 但我確實做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授們傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸 , 沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給了我一個反應 , 給了我憂鬱症讓我感到自殺 。 我記得: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 不久後 , 她聽過那位俄羅斯 , 一名全國的記者 , 一直在談我在國家t.v 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一本關於我父親的命運 , 他死後的一年 , 當時是泰姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做這個演說節目 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 , 最初的俄羅斯 , 位於 「 會議 」 , 談到我的寫作 , 我在沃爾瑪停車的車上 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 是因為那時候 , 我是作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書中 。 我找到了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡了 。 我把我的命運放回去 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友一起改變生活 。
and i started writing again .	我再次寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	在接下來的年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏了獎勵 。 我自己住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人都在工作和參與工作 , 生活在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續被忽略並犯罪 , 在你的車輛或街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 主要是保持隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇過一個人 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	如果有希望的話 , 人類的精神能克服任何東西 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是要成為無家可歸的女生 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你們給你下一個panhandler的錢給你 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是生活在哪裡 , 他們睡在哪裡 , 或生活情境在任何時刻 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一個沃爾瑪停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠 , 總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 " mr. " 音樂 " 中 , 墨西拉哈維亞 , 帶著我們走過國家大膽的計畫 , 從1970年代開始 , 第一步開始 , 人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克、非常有趣的和非常有效的談話 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球性議題、健康、科學、科學、科學和社會 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	梅拉蒂亞:mr.保險套如何讓泰國變得更好的地方 , 讓泰國更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 我還是個年輕人 , 國家非常非常貧窮 , 許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們沒有從福利計畫或貧窮的計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭平台開始 , 追隨一個非常成功的女兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:去找孩子 , 來到母親 , 然後跟著家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我回顧一下為什麼我們要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭中的七個孩子在3.3%的成長 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	我們說: 「 咱們來做 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來準備藥丸 。 」 我們有非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有作為一個答案 , 我們沒有一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和候選人 , 他們也是女性 , 做了一件很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那真是太棒了 , 但它只包含了20%的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其它80%離開他們 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了你所見的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	實際上 , 黃色的標誌下方 , 我希望他們沒寫過 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那些日子我們比可口可樂更大 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選擇的人是我們選的 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中被知名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們是很恐怖的 , 他們練習了他們的家庭規劃自己 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供給全國各地的藥和保險套 , 在全國各地的村莊 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們去了 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的原因 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不管哪裡有人 , 你都能看到那些女人的船 , 賣東西是漂浮的市場銷售香蕉和螃蟹 , 不管你找到人 , 你會在泰國找到避孕性 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教堂很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裡 , 藍色的 , 不是黃色的黃色 , 讓僧侶有著一塊美麗的水 , 可以在藥丸和保險套 , 讓家人保持聖經 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片是全國各地的 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以 , 在村莊裡的一些僧侶都在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 不想我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它被賦予了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去了老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與 , 試著提供任何能讓人性更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過四十萬人被教導家庭規劃的家庭規劃 , 一個新的字母 , 一個新字母 , 出生 , 以外 , 我為伊德 , 為主動詞 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	接著 , 我們有一顆蛇和雷射遊戲 , 你丟掉掉掉掉掉 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何預期規劃上降落 , 你就搬到前面 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	例如: 「 母親每天晚上都會吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 向前移動 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了一套保險套 , 非常好 , 叔叔 , 往前移動 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝酒 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再一次 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	再一次 , 教育、課堂娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套相關的種族 , 我們有孩子的同意冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久以前 , 國會被認為是女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對於窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓它變得如此 , 內容是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們介紹了1975年的第一項微型編輯計畫 , 那些組織的女性說: 「 我們只想把家庭規劃的女性交給女子 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們跑的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年後 , 它仍在發生 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 而是一個基金的微型設備 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個很大的組織 , 來處理它 , 是因為村民本身運作 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能看不到泰國的男人 , 總是女人、女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每個人 , 不論他們想要幫助或不想幫助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月第四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定提供所有男人的昆蟲 , 但尤其是 , 美國男子前面 , 位於大使館的住宅 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們這個房間 , 讓它非常適當的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	自從那近午餐時 , 他們說: 「 好 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的煤炭 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你得到兩個品牌 , 可樂和pepsi 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	接著 , 食物是漢堡或熱門 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我覺得很熱 , 會更符合象徵 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是這個 , 年輕人叫威廉博士 , 他為美國大屠殺工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他的動作是因為他的熱量是半個飲食 , 他很開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國製造了很多新聞 , 它也激發了一些人 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 再過來 , 我會做很多人 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	這一切 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是相同的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不知道可口可樂是否跟著我們 , 或者我們遵循可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是所有人都參與的案例 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有一個堅強的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	然後愛滋病來到達泰國 , 我們必須停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的作品並沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍事 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以 , 我去了軍隊 , 請求借三百個電台站 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們比政府更有槍 , 比政府更有槍 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們可以幫助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據之後 , 他們說: 「 是的 。 你可以用所有的無線電站、電視站 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	這就是我們去了空氣波的時候 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	之後 , 我們得到了一個新的總理 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 梅西 , 你能來加入嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他問我 , 因為他喜歡我的妻子 。
so i said , " okay . "	所以我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為國家援助委員會的主席 , 增加預算的五十倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都必須參與愛滋病教育 , 我們說了公共、機構、宗教機構 , 每個人都參與 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	然後我們決定幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們就得以解決問題 , 而不是單單靠政府 , 而是與商業社區合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是缺乏商業技能的人 , 取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些是商業社群提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們轉變成創業家 , 小企業家 , 小企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	貧窮唯一的方法是透過商業企業企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 這已經完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	貨幣從公司進入村莊的村莊 。

they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們植物樹木 , 金錢到他們的微型成本基金 , 我們稱之為村莊發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人加入 , 他們覺得他們擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你能借錢之前 , 你得要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮的人 , 相信信用必須要是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用必須要是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	到達貸款之前 , 你一定要被訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 嬰兒mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣做 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功 。

they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止製造鞋和衣服 。

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何人坐著看著電視 , 跟我一起接觸 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 最後 , 在教育方面 , 我們想要改變學校 , 把學校被被污染到一個地方 , 它是一生的學習中心 。
