your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像個朋友 , 但真的朋友會在ted2013年 , 在ted2013年 , 克里娜•羅馬 , 智慧型機器人可以在路上移動 , 把你放在桌上 , 把咖啡放在桌上 , 反應給你 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	克里娜•里納多:一個由你的手機發電的小機器人權力 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	只要舉手舉手 , 你們有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不太多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	沒錯 , 實際上 , 如果你不包含房間 , 有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們試圖解決的問題 , 我和其他20個浪漫的神經 , 都很迷人於解決解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以 , 我們真的想要建造一個人可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八、八、八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個很困難的問題 , 因為你必須建立一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不只能負擔得起的機器人 , 而是人們真的想要帶回家 , 並在孩子周圍 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人無法被忽視或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	羅馬的機器人 , 你已經知道和愛你的iphone 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由控制iphone處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造出一個可以維持一百五十美元的機器人 , 這大約有百分之一的機器人在過去的代價 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當羅馬上升時 , 他正處於生物模式 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上用了影片攝影機來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我倒下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很勇敢 , 所以他會把眼睛留在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來這裡 , 他會跟著我說話 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就很害怕其他生物 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 很多方面來說 , 羅馬就像他自己的想法一樣 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探究世界uh , 羅馬的累積如果我想用romo來探索世界 , 我真的可以將他與其他ios設備聯繫起來 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	羅馬會把影片帶到這個裝置上 。

if i get in front of romo here .	如果我站在羅馬前面 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我就可以開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	我可以把他帶到旁邊 , 我可以拍攝你們的照片 。

and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	同樣的 , 透過ipad的內容 , 我可以調整儀器上的鏡頭角 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	各位都穿過羅馬的眼睛 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒表達自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以 , 我可以進去 , 我可以說 , 讓我們做romo興奮 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但最重要的是 , 我們想要創造一個完全直覺的事物 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教別人如何驅動romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰想開一個機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不需要在同樣的地理位置 , 以機器人來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以 , 他實際上是兩位聰明的儀器和影片 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以透過瀏覽器運輸 , 有點像是在輪椅上 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以 , 我們在討論關於電視之前 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 舉例來說 , 誰有iphone , 她媽媽買了她的機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以帶她iphone , 把它放到機器人上 , 送一封電子郵件給祖母 , 他住在國的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那個機器人 , 和她祖母一起玩 , 每晚五十五分鐘 , 否則她只能看到她的祖母一次或一年兩倍 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以 , 這些是今天可以做些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們在未來工作的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們其中一個工程師 , 一週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它建在google開放式架構上 , 叫做 「 封鎖 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以開車 , 把這些區塊放到你想要的機器人上 , 創造出任何一種行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以模擬在瀏覽器裡的行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到羅馬正在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	若你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以在機器人上下載它 , 在現實生活中執行它 , 在現實生活中執行這個計畫 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你自豪的東西 , 你可以和世界上的其他機器人分享它 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wifi的機器人其實都能從彼此學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們專注於建造機器人的原因是 , 所有人都可以訓練的原因是 , 我們認為 , 個人機器人的使用案件是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人到人身上改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	我們認為如果你在家裡有一個機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們知道的是 , 不是10億美金或100億美金或大型人類機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	現今 , 個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它會仰賴小型、小型的機器人 , 例如romo , 以及像你這樣的人 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及給你所有機器人 , 我們等不及你建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和激進主義者 , 討論女性、創意、定義女性、女性主義 , 當然 , 也是這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、父母、說故事、女人、世界文化、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾說出熱情的味道 , 是關於熱情的味道 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 真的很可怕 , 在這裡是智慧最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡告訴各位一些熱情 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我喜歡的 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼是真相呢 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 。 我想說的是 , 比我們常見的人性真相的真實性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 有些傷害我 , 直到我最後寫了他們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些人會說:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的神秘 , 所以我寫了關於巧合、偏好、情感、夢想、大自然的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我已經活在2006年2月 , 直到2006年2月 , 我在義大利奧運中帶著奧運旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為一個慶祝 。 現在 , 人們認知我 , 我祖父認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來告訴各位我四分鐘的名字 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克的一個組織者 , 叫做 「 開放的儀式 」 , 叫我 , 說 , 我被選擇成為一個旗幟家之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我重覆了 , 肯定這是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我可以從一個運動員身上得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我能在沒有行者的房間裡走進場 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知 , 這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這將會是第一次 , 只有女人會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女人 , 代表五大洲 , 三個奧林匹克的金屬贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 天然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一個單位 , 她說 , 請求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我在一個流感的理論中有一種視覺 , 看起來像米林的男人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	在二月的中間 , 我發現我自己在土耳其 , 在那裡 , 當任何八十個奧林匹克隊都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但有幸運的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一股雪、一英吋的冰、風力 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或幸運是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有一個無害且決定的心會得到金額的金額 。
it is all about passion .	重點是熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅色海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運的邏輯 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心臟驅使我們並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在書中所需要的角色:一個熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要大眾、孤獨、冒險家、外國人、叛軍 , 他們問問題、規則和冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座的各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	享受共同感的好人 , 不是創造有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會製造好的配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在演室的綠色房間 , 我遇見了另一個旗幟熊:三位運動員 , 和索爾尼亞倫敦 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 兩位有熱情心心的婦女:威爾•馬達 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 由此 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲 , 當然 , 許多村落的經濟條件 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	馬上媽媽 , 一位柬埔寨的活動家 , 他對抗兒童機構的熱情 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 她的祖父賣給她的兄弟 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男性強暴 , 相信有性愛和很年輕的維吉文會治癒他們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	孩子們每天被迫接收五、十五、十五位客戶 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們就被迫被迫被強迫了 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色的房間裡 , 我收到我的單位 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我常穿的好處 , 而是從我預期的米蘭人的米西林 , 不是很糟糕的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 大部分的旗幟 , 除了索菲亞•倫敦 , 美麗和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲亞超過七十歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她是性感、刺激 , 有著深度的尾巴 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你要如何有深度的尾巴 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪談時 , 「 她怎麼看得太好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 海報 。 我的背總是直直 , 我不讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有抓住 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有頭髮 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有太遠 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒說過這一點 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	今晚 , 我們總結了這場球場的翅膀 , 大聲宣佈了奧林匹克•旗幟 , 音樂始於此 , 相同的音樂開始 , 愛滋亞馬克 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	索菲亞•洛倫在我面前 , 她比我還高 , 不算是好頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她很明顯地走路 , 像非洲大草原一樣 , 握著她的肩膀的旗幟 。 我在我的手臂背後抓住了旗幟 , 所以 , 我的頭其實在達爾斯旗下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有攝影機都在索菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在我看到的大部分的媒體照片中 , 雖然經常是蘇菲洲的腿 。
a place where most men would love to be .	大部份人會想成為一個地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最好的四分鐘就是奧林匹克的場所 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我丈夫在說這句話雖然我向他解釋了 , 私人所做的通常要花不到四分鐘 , 讓他不該個人做這件事 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四個偉大的時刻 , 因為我不想忘記他們 , 因為當老年破壞我的大腦細胞時 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想帶著我的心臟 , 永遠是奧林匹克熱情的關鍵詞 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這是一種熱情的味道 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 那個地方是剛果的蘇聯難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上有80%的難民和殘疾的人是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為 「 剛果營 」 , 因為那些沒有殺死疾病或飢餓的人會死亡 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕的女士 , 羅斯•格蘭多 , 她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和一扇窗戶 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她去看她的丈夫 , 被迫害 , 被殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼地 , 她能讓七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她會出生 , 來做早期的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她把腫瘤皮膚切割成黏著 , 用牠自己的頭髮 ,
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她在營區的指揮後命名叫 「 雙胞胎 」 , 用黑茶餵給他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法保持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的細胞內埋葬在她最老的女兒 , 她抓住了她 , 拒絕放棄 , 即使他們拿著槍給她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不管怎樣 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 經過了不凡的幸運 , 一個年輕的美國人的熱情心 , 他們在美國救援飛機上 , 羅斯•格蘭多和她的九個兒童終於活在鳳凰身上 , 他們現在活著和茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖 , 在瓦希里 , 意思是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書的主角是強烈且熱情的女性 , 像是roe地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不想把它們弄出來 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我四周看 , 看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我和女性和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我知道他們很好 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古時期 , 在世界末端 , 在一個專業的天主教和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪 , 五歲時 , 我是個強暴的女性主義者雖然這名詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我是錯的 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 對於我自由有很高的價格 , 為了質疑 「 專利 」 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興要付錢 , 因為對於我收到的每一塊 , 我都能提供兩個 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	一旦 , 我女兒保羅在她的二十歲時 , 她對我說 , 女權主義被約會 , 我應該繼續 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一對不可思議的鬥爭 。 女性主義是被約會的嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒一樣的特權女性 , 今天我們所有人 , 但在世界上大部分的姊妹 , 仍然強迫婚姻 , 賣淫 , 她們有她們不想要或無法餵食的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制他們的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育和自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被殺害 , 有時被殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	今天大部分的西方年輕婦女 , 被稱為女權主義者是侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性愛 , 但讓我保證它永遠不會阻止我 , 讓我感到失望 , 我有缺乏男人 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義不是死了 , 不管如何 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 改變神的樣本 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 孤獨 」 , 或 「 bimbo 」 , 或任何你想要的東西 , 都不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一種熱情的味道 , 這是一個悲傷的 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	在孟加拉村的一個小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	今年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫醫師 , 在她三維假期間 , 一位志願者就去診所 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備乾淨牙齒 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一場漂亮的果蠅 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一系列的婦女 , 等了好幾個小時才能被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位患者是非常精確的痛苦 , 因為她有幾條旋轉的分子 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一的解決方案就是把壞牙齒拉出來 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她不是這樣做 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很多風險 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶了一些小說 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她媽媽媽媽媽媽媽媽媽媽媽跟著手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 放棄病人的雙手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 海吉主義者把更多牙齒拉出來 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人在等著她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像水母 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮在她做的事很害怕 , 但後來翻譯者解釋 , 病人的條件是沒有關係的 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打敗了她 , 因為她沒有回家 , 為了為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬女性生活在這樣的情況下 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人最窮的 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性有三分之二的勞工 , 他們擁有世界上的資產只有百分之一 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水較少於男性 , 如果他們付出的錢 , 且他們保持脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 他們會不斷威脅 , 被剝奪、暴力和虐待 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	這個事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制他們的收入、自私、自己的財產、受益社會的能力 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭專家 , 村民的教授 , 最終 , 整個國家的確是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	塔里馬利馬利在肯亞的村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人說話 , 解釋 , 土地是灰色的 , 因為他們被砍掉 , 賣掉樹 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她得到了女性來種植新的樹和水 , 下降了 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五年或六年裡 , 他們有森林 , 土壤被強化了 , 村莊被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最後面的社會總是把女性放下去 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這很明顯的真理被政府忽略 , 也被慈善事業所忽視 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一美元給婦女專案 , 20美金給男性的專案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是百分之五十一的人 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們能改變所有東西 , 比科技和設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起合作 , 聯繫和教育 , 可以將和平和繁榮帶給這個星球 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的習慣都是平民 , 主要是婦女和孩子 。 他們是冷漠的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人逃離世界 , 看看我們有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	能否參與現有的世界秩序嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 生命是保存和生活品質的 , 對每個人來說 , 不僅僅是特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我看到了佛羅•波里奧的畫作在柏克萊圖書館的展覽 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或gallery , 除了紐約galry的作品 , 可是criceo的作品 , 卻敢展示這幅畫 , 因為這個主題是abuhraib監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的細節和濫用權力的大幅畫 , 在大量的瓶子裡 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把這些影像從我的腦中得到 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是有責任的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力濫用 , 且濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性雄性定義現實 , 迫使其餘的背景接受現實和遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則一直都改變 , 但他們總是受益 , 在這個案例中 , 驚人的效應 , 沒有在經濟上運作 , 完美地運作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待障礙從拉德的頂端到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 在底部 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最絕望的男人 , 她們能虐待一個女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我對許多性別、收入、和階級的權力有著較少的權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間在我們的文明中做出基本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能源 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一個關鍵的女性 , 在權力的位置 , 我們需要培養女性的能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我在談的是年輕的腦袋 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人是無希望的 ; 我們得要等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	沒錯 , 我很喜歡有索菲利亞的長腿和法律的乳房 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 有一個選擇 , 我寧願有了大麻的戰士心 , 湯瑪麗瑪麗 , 珍妮和羅斯地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不好 , 但要讓它變得好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為何不 ? 看看這間房間裡的知識、能源、智慧和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們來脫離我們的寶寶 , 滾起我們的袖子 , 去工作 , 熱情地 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市中 , 三千萬個餐廳被服務了 。 但所有食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築石油的奇蹟指出 , 每天的餵養一個城市 , 展現古老的食物路是如何塑造現代世界的 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡林林爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們當時最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們把它放進一間店或餐廳裡 , 還是在一小時內 , 大約一小時內 , 會有食物 , 等待我們 , 有魔法從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每一天 , 倫敦大小的城市 , 足夠的食物要被生產、運送、買賣、吃飯、吃掉、吃掉 , 每一天都能發生 , 都市的每一大城市都能得到驚人的食物 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 如同他們是世界上最自然的事物 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 我們其實是依賴自然世界的依賴我們的古祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們更多人搬進城市 , 自然世界被轉化為非凡的地景 , 像我背後的那一塊 , 它在巴西的曼德羅西地區 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但我們少數人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多這些景觀 , 不僅僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們更多人搬到城市 , 更多人吃肉 , 所以 , 全球有三分之一的農作物現在已經被餵養到動物 , 而不是人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	因爲它需要花了三倍的穀物 , 才能餵飽人類 , 如果它是通過一隻動物的第一種 , 那不是非常有效率的餵養我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個令人困惑的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 估計我們居住在城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	它也估計 , 將有兩倍的肉和鳥類消耗 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉和都市主義在手上騎手 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會造成巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到了2050年 , 六十億的飢餓屍體來餵食 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 , 實際上 , 如果我們帶著我們 , 我們很有可能解決這個問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	九十萬英畝的雨林每年都失去了新的原住地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然在同一時間 , 我們也失去了平等的存在量 , 以致於鹽化和排放 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對化石燃料也非常飢餓 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要10個卡路里來製造我們在西方消耗的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們在偉大的成本中有食物 , 我們其實不珍惜它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半的糧食已經消失了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	最後 , 在這個長期的過程結束 , 我們甚至沒有適合適合餵飽地球的糧食 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們有十億人肥胖 , 同時有十億顆恆星 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有任何東西都很合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 80%的全球貿易現在是僅僅僅5個跨國企業 , 它是一張最悲慘的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是不穩定的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	那麼 , 我們怎麼來到這裡 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做呢 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	嗯 , 先稍微簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程在古老的東邊 , 所謂的肥料 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	這也是肥料 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這裡有兩萬個非凡的發明 , 農業和都市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也發生了 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外的 , 因為農業和城市是有限的 , 他們需要彼此的 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為它發現了我們古老祖先第一次產生食物來源 , 足以支撐永久的地位 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些地方是什麼樣子 , 我們看到它們是相對的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產的農場包圍 , 被大型寺廟所主導 , 例如這個 , 實際上 , 事實上 , 精神化、中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為它是組織了收穫的寺廟 , 聚集在穀物上 , 給上帝 , 然後提供了神的穀物 , 給予神不吃的人民 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你想 , 整個城市的靈性和身體生活都由穀物和樹木所佔據 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古代城市的確如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都很小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	一世紀初 , 羅馬有大約一百萬公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼樣的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古老食物哩 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬接觸到海 , 讓它可以從非常遙遠的距離運動食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界中唯一能做到的唯一方法 , 因為要把食物運送到路上 , 路上是非常困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	很明顯地 , 食物很快就發生了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地在像照顧和埃及的地方寫下戰爭 , 只能在他們的穀物儲存中得到它的尾巴 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張是很長的 , 引起軍事購物的速度 , 真的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到:羅馬在倫敦的摩西斯特 , 在一個階段 , 我覺得這很不尋常 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬的形狀 , 透過它的蘋果來形塑它 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 在工業界也發生了另一件事情 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看17世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 來自thames , 在這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場到城市南部 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從他們到便宜 , 到廉價 , 這是主要的市場 , 也是有穀物的市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看那些街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你就可以知道三百年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 對魚而言也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也來自河流 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billsgate , 是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期中期 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	很不凡 , 當你想到它時 , 這真是太棒了 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他的所有人都在移動手機旁邊 , 看起來像磚塊 , 有點像魚類 , 在葡萄牙發生 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市的食物的另一件事:一旦它根根部落到城市中 , 它們很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是非常不同的故事 , 因為 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的肉來自北極 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾蘭 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以 , 到達北方的城市 , 到達北方的城市 , 這就是為什麼密西斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常著名的肉市場 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	農業從東角來 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我感覺有點像天氣女人這樣做 。 無論如何 , 鳥會用牠們的腳來保護牠們的腳趾 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當他們撞到便宜的東端時 , 這就是他們賣的原因 , 這就是為什麼它被稱為 「 文化 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何城市在工業時代建造的地圖 , 你可以把食物帶到它上來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所形塑的 , 透過閱讀街道的名字 , 讓你有許多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五的街道 , 在過去的人生中 , 你在星期五買了魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也得想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一能買的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們在1830年看一幅smithfield的影像 , 你可以看到 , 在像這樣的城市中 , 你的食物從哪裡來是非常困難的 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在星期五午餐時 , 機會就在你的窗外或在你的窗外打破 , 大約三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這很顯然是一個有機的城市 , 其中一部分是有機循環 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年的偉大西方的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 有些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被拒絕了視覺和思想 , 在一個國家的某個地方 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們是從鐵達來的城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它是有可能的 , 要是第一次成長城市 , 真正的大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前 , 城市曾經被地理所限制 ; 他們以前必須透過非常困難的實體體來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們的確是從地理上開始的 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦的這些地圖中看到 , 在火車的90年後 , 它從一個小小的鳥身上餵食 , 很容易被動物吃掉 , 所以 , 到一個大的蜘蛛 , 很難餵飽任何人在腳上 , 無論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是一開始 。 火車來到車後 , 真的是這個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是整個城市的最終融合 , 來自任何與大自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市是聞聞聞的味道 , 絕對是人 , 因為沒有人會想在這樣的地景上走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們所做的是把食物帶到車子裡 , 帶到一個盒子裡 , 帶著一週的購物 , 回來了 , 想著地球上怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是當我們和食物和城市之間的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡 , 我們有食物可以成為中心 , 城市的社交核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它曾經是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們曾經煮飯 , 現在我們只加水 , 或有點蛋 , 如果你在做蛋糕或一些蛋 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們剛剛讀了一份標籤的後面 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不珍惜食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不相信它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評價 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代的食物系統之一 , 其中一個偉大的諷刺是 , 他們讓他們承諾更容易做得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓它可以在任何地方建立城市 , 並且在我們最重要的關係中 , 我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 他們也讓我們依賴系統 , 只能傳遞給我們 , 如同我們所見 , 無法永續發展的系統 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那麼我們要怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 湯瑪斯更問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的前列 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列的獨立城市 , 如果那聽起來很熟悉 , 一天 , 每一天 , 每個人都被養殖 , 成長了蔬菜 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你可以爭論食物是烏托邦的基本秩序原則 , 儘管更多人從來沒有這樣做 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 視覺 , 伊貝尼斯•霍華 , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:一系列的獨立城市 , 一小塊大陸的小塊 , 帶著安裝的土地 , 加入另一塊鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣地 , 食物可以成為他的視覺的秩序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至建構了 , 但沒有什麼關係 , 可是 , 和霍華的視覺有關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這是這些烏托邦的想法 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯摩爾用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它是來自希臘的兩倍 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	不論是好的地方 , 還是沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 , 這是一種想像力的東西 , 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我想 , 身為一個概念工具 , 來思考人類dwilling的深度問題 , 讓它不太用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出一個替代方案 , 是西亞 , 來自古希臘 , 《西班牙》、 「 食物 」 和 「 popos 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經活在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個充滿食物的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以把食物當作一個有力的工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式形塑世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們要這樣做 , 西托邦會是怎樣的 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是看狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生活中心的食物 , 在家庭生活中心 , 被慶祝 , 被享受 , 人們花時間去做 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是食物應該在我們的社會中 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但 , 除非你有像這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便一提 , 這些都是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 想前面的 , 他的計畫 , 誰可以盯著一堆大型的拖延蔬菜 , 真的認出他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就不能這樣做 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我會選擇這個 , 因為這是一個人買蔬菜的男人 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但 , 網絡 , 食物在當地成長的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	這是城市的社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為如果沒有這樣 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地的食物也就是土地的一部分 , 而不只是一個無限的商品 。
cows with a view .	用一個觀點來煮牛 。
steaming piles of humus .	尖叫著幽默 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	基本上 , 把整個東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多的社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一個溫室 , 孩子們都知道食物和生長自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一個叫做kevin的植物 , 或者 , 它是種叫做kevin的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但 , 總之 , 這些計畫試圖將我們和大自然重新連結在一起 , 是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 對我來說 , 是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到 , 西班牙已經存在於小袋子裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	技巧是加入他們 , 用食物作為一種看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就停止看到城市 , 大到大 , 大都市 , 沒有生產力的爆炸 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將更像這樣的看法 , 身為生產力、有機框架 , 他們不可避免的一部分 , 相對的連結 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣的生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要思考更多關於文化的觀念 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖片是為了我認為我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種對食物形狀的概念化 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是從650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	它是艾布羅維多•倫維蒂的 「 良好政府的盟友 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和國家之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息是非常清楚的 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市在全國看後 , 國家會回顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我希望我們現在要問 , 如果他今天畫了這張圖片 , 該怎麼辦 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府會怎樣 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的就是我們吃的 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解到 , 世界也是我們吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個強大的工具來形塑世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	從同情推出的幾個星期 , 肯亞阿拉伯•阿姆斯壯看二十一世紀的宗教角色:它的狗會將我們分裂嗎 ? 還是會讓我們很喜歡嗎 ? 她反映了世界上的信仰 , 來重新定義黃金規則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009年、暴力事件、暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenstrong:咱們來拯救黃金規則規則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我感到挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我真的意識到所有主要世界的同情心核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出自己的版本 , 叫做黃金規則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它會出現在正面版本上 , 「 總是對待別人 , 就像你想要治療自己一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面版本是 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡的事 」 。
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現它會讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 衝突任何人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來好 , 而是因爲它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們把黃金規則當作混亂說: 「 每天和每一天 , 不只一個你好好的做法 , 然後回復一輩子 , 但每天都要做 , 你將自己從你世界的中心拿出來 , 將自己轉換成你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶著你進入所謂的 「 神 」 、nirvana、rama、tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	除了我們在演算法的存在中所知的事物 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠不知道它 , 這對宗教生活非常重要 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些奇妙的例外 , 當宗教人聚集在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們爭論抽象的劑量 , 或猶豫的仇恨 , 或對抗同性戀 , 或這種類型 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常 , 人們並不想要同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	有時 , 我會看到當我跟宗教人士說話時 , 有點像突顯他們的臉孔 , 因為人們常會想做對立 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	而那當然會破壞運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我很感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們讓我很高興地從我的書籍研究帶到21世紀 , 讓我能和一個更廣泛的觀眾說話 , 比我曾經想像過的還要多 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到緊急 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不成功地把黃金規則實施到全球 , 所以 , 我們對所有人 , 無論他們是哪些人 , 無論他們是誰 , 我都懷疑我們有可行的世界來對下一個世代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們時代的任務之一是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說的 , 人們可以一起生活在和平之中 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只宗教人士相信金屬規則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種想像力的行為 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 似乎對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們能否帶出去或強調我們信仰的信仰 , 或我們可以回到拉比爾 , 阿比比比爾 , 老的耶穌 , 當他在一支猶太教學時 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 他說: 「 這對你的鄰居來說是很討厭的 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這是湯瑪拉和其他的一切 , 只有評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教堂的早期父親 , 說 , 任何文字的詮釋 , 都被破壞了仇恨和失落 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要拯救那個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	不只會發生 , 因為愛的靈魂會讓我們下降 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須實現這一點 , 我們可以用現代的溝通來做 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經在我們所有夥伴的回應中被強烈的心臟關注 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人 , 將使用法案來治癒 , 最近 , 在新加坡社會中 , 有些國會想要在政治上實現 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬拉西亞 , 會有一個藝術展覽 , 領導藝術家將要帶到人們、年輕人 , 展現同情心 , 展現所有藝術的根部 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	橫跨歐洲 , 穆斯林社區有活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰的核心核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它無法停下來 , 它無法停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 這就是我們已經錯了 , 堅信抽象的教學 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我很想在這個臨終的日子上工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想和我們的夥伴們一起做兩件事教育和刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們已經脫離同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常認為這對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但 , 當然 , 你不了解同理心 , 如果你只是想它 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 協助分解一些我們有其他人的刻板印象 , 將我們分成彼此 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣應用於教育家 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到動態、動態和挑戰同情的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到 , 它需要特定的智能 , 不只是一個高興的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 去探索他們自己的同理心 , 在別人的傳統中 , 和其他人的傳統中 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 鼓勵一種對不同情的說話的敏感 , 所以 , 因爲人們有這個信念 , 不論他們都沒有信念 , 他們都被賦予挑戰不安的言論 , 從他們的宗教領袖、政治領袖、政治領袖 , 來自產業的領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把圖表放在線上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊世界裡 , 一大堆的框架中 , 坐在房間裡 , 還在另一條北極的陳述中 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted介紹了我全新的思想和展示想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的美好 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專家 , 如果我們一起加入 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎是可行的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我只是想引用 , 最後最後 , 最後 , 一個英國作者 , 一位牛津作家 , 我不常引用c.lewi 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 自從我讀書時 , 一直在我還是學術時 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	他的書是《四個愛》 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他在愛情之間分散 , 當兩個人聚集、拼字 , 到彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	然後他跟朋友相比 , 當兩個人站在旁邊時 , 肩膀肩膀 , 眼睛在共通目標上固定 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要互相愛 , 但我們能成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我說服了 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我感覺到在我們的調查中非常強烈 , 當所有不同的說法的人聚在一起時 , 一起工作 , 一邊是常見的目標 , 差異會消失 。
and we learn amity .	我們學到了正義 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝大家 。

removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	移除一些腳踏車 。 其中一個原因之一是 , 羅馬仍然保持了不起的位置 , 原因之一是 , 原因是 , 要維持公平的結構 , 它是一個持續成長並適應它的需求 , 或我們發現它本身 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	通過帕薩德拉德拉•羅頓達 , 在前面 , 再次在威脅哈利克 , 終於開始工作 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	馬里羅 , 結果是數字64公車的駕駛 , 如果你在數字64公車上 , 你知道它的開車和火星在他的分數上展示一樣 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後卡萊托 , 你看到他在左上角的公寓 。
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他在看他的桌子 , 他要建議他40年的女友 , 他希望它是完美的 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他有蠟燭 , 中間有一朵花 , 他試著想出要把盤子和玻璃放到哪裡 。

he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他在一個好的影片中遇見 , 但比起我們剛剛所見的旅程 , 他正在碰到的都市 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道卡萊托 , 因為他在娛樂中 , 事實上 , 他在電視中 。

he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他抵達保羅 , 抵達大門的前門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入法院和客戶交談 , 告訴他 , 在palazzo有一個災難 ; 沒有人的電視都在工作 , 上面有一場巨大的足球 , 群眾變得有點無限 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走向地下去 , 開始檢查出生 , 然後慢慢地工作 , 到公寓的頂端 , 公寓 , 檢查每次電視 , 檢查所有聯繫 , 請找出這個問題 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他在路上工作 , 終於 , 大樓樓梯 , 之後 , 一個較小的樓梯 , 直到他抵達了票 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	當然 , 他打開了大樓的窗戶 , 上面有一張桌子在建築的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除了它 , 問題已經解決了 , 在巴拉茲的每個人都很開心 。

all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要做 , 用完美的桌子 , 等著她來到達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一個嘗試 , 但它似乎不夠細微 , 去探討我想要傳達羅馬的事物 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 嗯 , 我會做piazzas , 我會進到內部 , 向下展示這些東西的成長 , 展示為什麼他們被塑造了它們的樣子等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我心想 , 這太複雜了 , 不 , 我會把我最喜歡的小片和碎片放進箱子裡 , 我會把它們放進箱子裡 , 保持規模 , 這樣你就可以看到聖誕節和巴拉德的溫度和寺廟 , 在這個令人驚奇的空間中 ,
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這張圖是一張圖 , 所以我想 , 也許是piransi要見到escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看 , 我開始失去控制 , 同時也希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一個非常小的藍色的外交線 , 它會透過這種東西來運作 , 這種軌道會被整合起來 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等一下 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是收集和儲存資訊的好方法 , 而是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是一層一層 , 我們把它們視為頁面 , 做一個特定的方式 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們當成層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一層層層層層層層 , 垂直層 , 我心想 , 好吧 , 只要我拿下一張頁面 , 就可以讓我在想 , 如果我把它當作正確的方式 , 讓我可以給你看一些層面的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	在羅馬大樓的牆上 , 大部分的建築物都包含了害怕 ; 數世紀以來 , 這些結構已經被改造了 , 而不是被破壞 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左邊做一頁摺疊 , 讓你放大它 , 你就看到我所謂的害怕組織的意思 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 它變成了較小的窗戶 , 因為壞人來到哪裡 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	全部的適應力都被埋在胃下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以拿出一張palazo的頁面 , 給你們看它的內部發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但更重要的是 , 我也能向各位展示這些巨大的石頭是什麼樣子 , 和所有巨大的石塊一樣 , 或假的石塊做成磚塊 , 比較常發生 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點像三維 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你們到一個狹窄的小街上 , 其中一個令人驚訝的偏差之一 , 用一個雙大的噴霧紙 , 如果你像我一樣 , 閱讀一本小書 , 你希望把你的頭放進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你在頭上拍下你的頁面 , 在那段短暫的時期 。

ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我完全不打開這本書 , 如果我剛開了九十度 , 我們就在前方看 , 看上方 , 更低的位置 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把這本書轉換成另一方面 , 我們正看著平方形的前方 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 不單是一本書 , 不是完全開放 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看起來很不可思議 。 我心想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以和唯一開放的書組合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進入了神殿內部 , 成長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點迷失了人類品質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 這一直是件好事 , 如果你想要讓人們注意一本書 , 並且在路上拿起資訊 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 pigeon的進步 」 讓我身為有技巧的標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果它是個活生的鴿子 , 它會被稱作 「 家的奇數 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但它是這個旅程 。
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一台編輯工作 , 用它 , 但它會是一趟旅程 , 讓羅馬的旅程 , 展現我喜歡羅馬的所有事物 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	它是教堂頂端的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	在日子裡 , 做正常的鴿子 , 回來 , 整個地方 , 都包含了雪花和綠色的網絡 , 沒有這種鴿子可以回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 要找到另一個地方 , 讓我可以透過我最喜歡的東西 , 我們先從最高的位置開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回到和家人一起生活 , 不一定是好事 , 但它會再次把鴿子帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一種人應該以某種方式參與 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老年人 , 花了他的生命 , 看著生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 讓他們很危險 , 並且他們和這個傢伙的朋友一起 , 學習為他做技巧 , 並在午餐時和像這樣的東西 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	這個老人和這些鴿子之間的真正鍵結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束後就很生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們把他的名字拼字 , 叫做aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	有一天 , 他們出生了三到四天 , 沒有看到他住在這個小垃圾桶裡 , 他們會發出他的名字和飛行 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有足夠的力量 , 一起爬上屋頂 , 所有的鴿子 , 一片紅色的氣球 , 等著他 , 帶著他走在城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了這點:當他失去了鴿子時 , 他會把那隻鴿子從城市牆壁的牆上拿出來 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬的客戶中 , 死者從來沒有埋在牆裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是一個非常小的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	那真的會很長一段路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我走過了 。 再一次 , 如果包裝不適用 , 如果故事不在任何地方 , 我剛剛想起了頭銜 , 希望 , 會把我踢在正確的方向上 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它會把焦點放在我身上 , 我甚至會做一份編輯頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題的頁面 , 最終引導了我解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女士的故事 , 她在城市的牆壁外發送訊息 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子正在飛到這裡 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	各位可以看出湯姆和罰單等等 , 順便一提 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你會看到鴿子的軌道 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它就變成了必要且有可能 , 試著去探討那個感覺會是什麼樣子的飛行 , 沒有實際移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過去 , 這些金字塔的金字塔似乎很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了最多的希望鴿子 , 不是這樣:它會帶著恐怖的路線 , 就是我覺得這本書在四頁之外延長這本書 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們圍繞著大學 , 過去聖誕節的教堂 , 希臘•瑪麗亞和海克力士的神殿 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和palazzzo的優秀設計 , 由米開朗基羅所設計的石頭 , 由哥倫敦的最狹窄的逃離 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們在柬埔寨的基礎上打開了 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向我的學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為它是完全的基礎化的任何規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一的觀點規則是 , 如果它看起來可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消費點在哪裡 , 火星和其他幾位在克雷蒙亞的朋友 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖誕節賽前面 , 以便是一場足球比賽的比賽正在發生 , 我們被足球撞擊 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是個很糟糕的幻覺 , 被足球撞擊 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:有聖誕節瑪麗亞帕斯 , 有一顆足球 , 有些鳥的翅膀發生了 , 所以我必須重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	假如你想看到聖誕節瑪麗亞•迪拉帕斯 , 這些書真的很有彈性 , 不可思議地轉換它 , 看它是另一種 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過盟友 , 我們可以看到紅線被捕捉到的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥會把自己拉過這個中世紀的大樓 , 剩下幾個中世紀的大樓 , 來到聖基地的教堂 , 四周 , 我們已經提到piazanavona , 經過了幾次 , 經過了兩次 , 穿越了四個河流 , 接著 , 經過了一片美妙的邊境 , 停止了26英呎的泥巴 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們可以在內部轉動 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們真的不需要擔心重力 , 在這個時刻 , 這樣繪畫就可以在任何程度上 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們得到一個很大的爆炸 , 不讓人意外地模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	穿過我所談到的催化劑 , 充滿了美麗的心臟裝置 , 進入了內部的牆壁 , 上面的 「 激進器 」 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們抵達了palazzo的法庭 , 這是我們的目的 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接通過法院進入一個小窗戶 , 有人在畫圖板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿移除訊息 ; 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的事是 , 事實上 , 鴿子剛剛拍攝的地圖 , 紅線在所有視覺中延伸 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要做的就是閱讀這些典範 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究員在自我組裝上工作 , 不用建造東西 , 我們就能創造出自己的東西 , 大部份dna組合的概念 。 它是在早期的舞台上 , 兔子告訴我們三項獨立的計畫 , 可能是自我組合未來的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天空的兔子:我們能製造出自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我要向各位展示我們創造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築和機器很快就會自我組裝、複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要向各位展示我相信目前的製造狀態 , 和一些自然系統相比 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前製造的狀態中 , 我們有二到五年半的摩天機 , 組裝時間是五十萬到百萬的零件 , 非常複雜 , 非常令人興奮的技術 , 在史黛爾、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器能帶我們進入太空 , 五年來 , 組合時間是250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看天然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈米秒內摺疊 , 或是dna , 我們可以在大約一小時重複複複複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們是非常有效率的 , 比我們所建造的任何東西還要有效率 , 比我們所能建造的更複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能量方面 , 它們更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎無法犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以為長壽修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統很有趣 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把這個轉換成我們的建設環境 , 那麼我們有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為這關鍵在於自我組合 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想把自我組裝在我們的身體環境中 , 我想有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的複雜性 , 以便是我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要把這分解成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們的建築如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可程式化的部分 , 可以用這個序列來摺疊 , 或重建 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 讓它能啟動 , 讓我們的部分可以從這個計畫中摺疊出來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的企業重複性 , 來確保我們成功地建立我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些計畫 , 我的同事和我在麻省理工學院工作 , 完成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一 , 是麥克勞和決策 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重建的機器人8公尺 。 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們用機械電設備來擁抱 , 感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼了你想要摺疊的東西 , 以一系列的角度為負面120、120、120、120、120 , 負面的120個 , 或轉換 , 你將這個序列傳遞到弦上 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每位單位都拿著它的信息 , 如此負面120 , 便會轉向那邊 , 檢查一下 , 然後把它傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是最棒的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 設計師在這個計畫上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的帶給光明:這真的很可怕嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美金 , 許多人小時來製造這八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能否大規模擴大嗎 ? 我們能否把機器人嵌入每一部分 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看著大自然 , 或被動地嘗試重建程式性 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它會更進一步 , 它會嘗試真正的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它將計算最基本的建築物集合起來 , 數位邏輯會直接進入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nandgate 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一台電梯 , 會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的輸入 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 就像你在建造你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前的磚塊開始 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚塊中開始加入 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它在它之前的做法和你說的 , 你想要做些什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 以下或下降 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以 , 在左手邊 , 「 1 , 1 , 輸入量等於0輸出 , 它會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 輸入是1輸出的 , 它會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有了所有資訊 , 包含了他們所建設的內容 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了完全的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被告知如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以有一些可以爬上去閱讀 , 並且可以在一個人身上發出輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接擁抱 , 沒有外部指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個項目叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們現在所擁有的最令人興奮的例子 。
