for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你所感受的是什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們在這個形式中做出決策 , 我們會稱他們為 「 禮物 」 , 因為他們焦點現在是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現況是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	一直在於 「 我過去經歷過的情況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們將稱之為 「 過去 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在的 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在預期後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們會稱它們為 「 未來 」 。 他們的焦點在什麼樣子上 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間矛盾 , 我想說 , 時間觀點的矛盾 , 是你做出的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 你有一個偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	嗯 , 其實有六個人 , 有兩種方式可以出現 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被遺忘 , 兩種方式來成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在過去 , 或被負擔 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可能是現代化的 , 叫做你專注於生命的喜悅 , 或現場主義者 , 不重要 , 你的生命是被控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可能是未來的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是透明的未來:名字是 , 生命從死後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理的靈活性 , 轉變時間的觀點 , 依賴這種情況的需求 , 那就是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最樂觀的時間是怎樣的 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度承認性 。 在未來 , 溫度上升 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	改善現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是在過去和現代主義下低落 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫時混合物是你從過去的背景中得到的樣子 。 你將你的家人、身份、自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來的翅膀到新目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你所得到的 , 是能源、能源 , 來探索自己、地方、人、人 , 感官 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何次的觀點都比正面積更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來能為成功犧牲什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭的時間 。 他們犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲時間 , 犧牲了個人的迫切期待 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了同性戀 , 她們犧牲睡眠 , 所以它會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們生活在工作上 , 成就和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted的一些人共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是南布朗克斯•蓋托的貧窮孩子 , 一位醫師家人都住在過去和現場 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡 , 身為一名未來的人 , 他們都做這些犧牲 , 因為老師被介入 , 讓我未來 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我 , 不吃馬拉夫 , 因為如果你等待你兩個人 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了 「 現代主義 」 , 我把焦點放在過去七十六歲 , 我比以前更有生產力 , 比我更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校的比率 , 將成癮者結合成青少年的健康 , 治理了魔術的策略 , 促進了永續發展和保育 , 減少有五十分之一的身體反抗 , 改變了自殺恐怖攻擊的恐怖分子 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是:許多生命的謎題 , 可以透過了解你的時間觀點和其他的事物來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	而這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今有多少人的頭條會在一百年內 ? 一百年 ? kirkcron的 「 長期消息 」 計畫 , 不僅僅是現今的重要數十年 , 甚至在ted2010年時 , 他的頭條很近期的頭條線 , 可以形塑我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球性的議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞是真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們在消息中淹沒了 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	僅僅僅是每年有三千五百萬個新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在漫長的過程中有多少故事會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期消息背後的點子 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個很長的基金會 , 由tedtster所創立的專案 , 包括kevinkelly和stewart品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們正在尋找的新聞故事 , 可能是現在的50到100 , 000年之久 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你看過那些過濾器的新聞時 , 很多是從路上降落的 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 要從a.p 。 去年 , 這會在十年內很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	在50或100年內 , 這會發生什麼事嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好的 , 這有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 過去的今年 , 最重要的故事是經濟 , 很快地 , 不久後 , 這種特定的衰退將會是古老的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 哪些故事對未來有差別 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 讓我們來看看科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	某天 , 小機器人會通過我們的血液修復物品 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	某天就已經存在了 , 如果你是老鼠 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	有些最近的故事:奈米粒子用真正的蜜蜂毒 , 它們會把基因送到大腦裡 ; 一個可以穿過人類身體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那麼資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在有麻煩今天的餵食了六十億人 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	昨天我們聽到的 , 有超過十億人飢餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國將恆星 , 沒有基因改造作物 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	很幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲有十億的研究 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會很不一樣 , 如果中國設立了廣告 , 他們就可能是這樣 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經過度了美國最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經把德國超越了德國 , 他們開始在孩子身上做dna測試 , 選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各種方法來推回我們所知的限制 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些最近的發現:阿根廷有一隻螞蟻 , 現在已經傳播到每一塊大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一種自主的機器人科學家 , 很快就不需要我們 , 科學也不需要我們 , 生命也不需要我們 ; 一顆微生物在120萬年後爆發 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 沒有我們 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但 , 今年的最大新聞報導是這個:在月球上找到的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓它變得更容易讓蟻群更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能 , 或在座的某個人可能會寫一個大的檢查 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:在漫長的跑步中 , 有些新聞比其他人更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡林普林科展出來自卡斯坦航行到土星 , 專注於其最大的月球、泰坦的土衛二 , 這似乎是拍攝冰冰的噴射 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	太空總署、設計、探索、科學、空間、科技、宇宙、視覺化的視覺化
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡林林•皮羅弗林 , 我們要滿足我們 , 來滿足我們 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的十八分鐘 , 我要帶你們到一個旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是你和我過去幾年的旅程 , 大約五十年前 , 人類第一次站在地球上 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那五十年裡 , 我們不僅僅在月球上設立實體的腳步 , 但我們已經將機械太空船分散到所有星球上 , 我們已經被登陸了 , 和彗星一樣 , 在此時 , 我們有了一艘太空船 , 我們有著太空船在它的行星上 , 身為行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人任務都是一個更大的人類旅程之一:旅程 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 了解我們的起源 , 以及地球 , 我們的地球 , 來到達它 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	太陽系的所有地方 , 我們可能去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 在1980年代初 , 我們已經坐下了土星 , 但土星的調查變得更獨立 , 從卡斯坦太空船到達七年之內 , 在2004年夏天的夏天 , 以來 , 旅行在西尼號太空船旅行的軌道上 , 進入了地球軌道的軌道 , 變成了人類在太陽的最遠的地方 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是富有的星球系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 顯然地分析 , 與這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 單靠研究ring , 我們就學到很多關於恆星的距離和氣體 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是一幅美麗的安德羅馬阿拉•尼布拉 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這是一塊美麗的小屋星系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝的 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是非常的一部分 , 也是一個比喻 , 為了更大的人類航空 , 來了解周圍的所有事物之間的連結 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我無法告訴你們我們 , 我們所學到的都是卡斯坦 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看我們過去兩年半的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要把兩個最令人興奮的故事集中在這個重大的探險探險探險進展中 , 我們已經在土星進行了兩年半 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星被一個非常大且多樣化的月球組合在一起 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	他們從幾公里遠離美國的大小 , 橫跨到美國 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們所拍攝的最美麗的照片 , 事實上 , 用一些月球來展現土星 。 這裡是石頭的土星 , 這裡是土星 , 展示節奏的邊緣 , 展示你 , 用垂直的泥土 , 用月底來呈現月球 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星的四十七月有兩個月球是站起來的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	而這些是泰坦和土衛二 。 泰坦是土星最大的月球 , 直到卡斯坦到達達那裡 , 是太陽系中最大的爆炸 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這是個很長的身體 , 有著很感興趣的人 , 看了行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個非常大、厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為是我們在地球上所存在的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 在太陽系中任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣大部分都是分子氮 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸的 , 除了它的大氣中被簡單的有機物質困擾 , 像是甲烷和乙醇 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在泰坦的大氣中升起 , 他們的產品結合在一起 , 組成零粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種零零是無可避免的 , 完全是全球和鼓舞的泰坦 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你無法看見我們眼睛在可見的地面上看到我們的眼睛 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些零粒子 , 在我們接觸到卡斯坦之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫柔地向地面向地面 , 並在一個厚厚的有機電池中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	如同泰坦一樣 , 泰坦 , 或石油 , 或石油 , 或是我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙醇 , 可以在泰坦的表面溫度下液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是將水傳到地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣中 , 它是可容忍的 , 因此 , 意識到這個環境會帶到整個奇怪的可能性世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在雲層上 , 上面有數百公里的夏季 , 預防任何陽光 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是3050度下方的0度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管如此冷 , 你可以在泰坦的表面下降下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在地球上 , 雨林的做法:它會帶著樹枝 ; 它形成河流和洞穴 ; 它可以創造出峽谷 ; 它可以在大型的底下池和螃蟹中橄欖 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以洗掉高山峰和山丘 , 到低地 , 停下來 , 再思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像泰坦的表面是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 泰坦的高鼻子 , 像地球深處的深處一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很酷 , 很糟糕 , 可能是雨水 , 你可能站在冰川的海岸上 , 米克萊根的傷害是痛苦的 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在加入卡斯坦的表面前所看到的景象 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在泰坦發現了什麼 , 雖然它在細節裡 , 都不像那個故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 像卡斯坦人一樣 , 像一個叢林的冒險是真的 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說的 , 它有著厚厚的大氣 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是titan , 由太陽的背景 , 和ring是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	然而 , 另一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪個 。 這是個非常大氣的大氣 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡斯坦有樂器可以透過這個大氣層看到的表面 , 我的相機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是亮和黑色區域 , 這大約是對我們來說的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這太神秘了:我們無法弄清楚我們在泰坦看到什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域時 , 你會開始看到一些我們不知道的東西 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石 , 但在泰坦的表面上有非常少的隕石 , 意思是 , 這是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來是昆蟲 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來就像是分離的 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線條 , 它就意味著有碎片 , 像是一個錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但 , 我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一個事件發生了許多人被視為卡斯坦的高速調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這是熱氣探測器的部署 , 歐洲的熱氣探測器 , 卡斯尼西尼在太陽系超過七年 。 我們將它帶到泰坦的大氣層 , 花了兩半的時間來描述表面 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只是想強調這個事件的重要性 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外在太陽系上登陸在人類歷史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我腦海中 , 這種事件應該被標記在美國和歐洲各地的各個城市中 , 都是如此的重要性 , 不幸的是 , 這不是案例 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	對另一個原因來說 , 這是個國際任務 , 這個事件在歐洲 , 在德國 , 慶祝慶祝慶祝 , 英國的英文 , 德國的英語和德國的英語 , 以及法國和義大利亞 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個移動的示範 , 說明 「 聯合國 」 的意思是:一個真正的國家結合在一起 , 為好的成就 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 它是一個很大的難以探索一個星球 , 來了解地球的系統 , 對所有人類歷史而言 , 已經無法想像 , 現在人類真的碰到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我的意思是 , 我剛剛剛談到它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	這是個很大的情感事件 , 我會個人忘記 , 而你也不應該 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但 , 總之 , 探測器的測量是下降的 , 它也採用了大氣的圖片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 關於toran的表面的第一張照片 。 這是我們所看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那是個震驚人的 , 因為我們希望那些照片從軌道上拍攝的照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是個不可思議的模式 , 一個地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這是一種延長的乾燥模式 , 只由液體流動形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以遵循這些頻道 , 你可以看到它們如何轉變 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們將這個頻道轉換成這個區塊 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你正在看著海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一些海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是16公里的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是8公里拍攝的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里 , 8公里 , 大約是飛行器 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要在美國拿一架飛機旅行 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	所以 , 這是你在泰坦航空的窗戶 , 當你在泰坦的表面上飛行時 , 你會看到這張照片 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器回到表面 , 我要給你們看 , 先生女士 , 先生先生 , 第一張從外太陽系中拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水泡 , 是的嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它在其中一個平面黑色區域 , 沒有洞察覺 。 所以這不是我們登陸的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的基本上是一片泥土平面的土地 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一種不穩定的地面 , 被液態甲烷困住 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	這可能是這個物質在我們看到的這些頻道中被洗掉 , 花了數十億年才能填補低利的鹼基 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是熱體探測器的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但是 , 我們的圖片中沒有任何標誌 , 甚至在熱帶的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們找到沙丘時 , 就會變得更困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好的 , 這是我們在泰坦的平等區域的電影 , 展示這些塵埃 。 這些是100公尺高的塵埃 , 由幾公里 , 分開 , 它們會延伸到哩程和哩程 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百個 , 到一千或1200英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是泰坦的沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或你不會得到塵埃 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	再一次 , 難以置信 , 沒有流體 , 直到終於 , 我們看到北極地區湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在南極的南極地區 , 有一個湖面的景象 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大概是拉克斯大小的湖泊 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 只有一週半前 , 我們飛過了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們在加勒比海的大小發現一個特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以這似乎是液體 , 我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節中 , 都顯然是泰坦的極端 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現titan是一個很棒的、神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但很奇怪 , 但有著像地球的地理形式 , 和一個巨大的地理多樣性 , 只是在太陽系的複雜性和富有價值的世界 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們去了土衛二 , 土衛二是一顆小月球 , 大約是一百大小 。 你可以在英格蘭的旁邊看到它的大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白的 , 它的表面很明顯是碎片的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個非常地質的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但 , 土衛二的母親被發現在南極 , 我們看到南極的南極 , 我們發現了這個脆弱的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組合 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	這些碎片是由有機材料組成 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個地區 , 南極地區 , 已經進化了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就像是發現地球上的南極 , 比熱帶還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們用額外的圖片 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片的噴泉是有用的 , 網絡粒子會延伸到太空中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張圖片拿出來 , 拿出來 , 我們看到這些噴射的光線傳送給質量 , 事實上 , 在其他的影像中 , 數千英里 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊在研究像這樣的圖像 , 就像這張一樣 , 想著其他的結果來自卡斯坦 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們在結論的結論中 , 這些噴泉可能是從水面下的液態水中排放出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有了 , 液態水 , 有機材料 , 和其他的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能在現代的行星探索上出現了 , 或換句話說 , 一個可能適合活生生生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明基因發生的不曾再一次 , 但在我們的太陽系中 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 宇宙中有著驚人的數量 , 宇宙中有137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是唯一的行星 , 仍然存在於生命中 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們所知唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在1960年代 , 任何人都在阿爾伯特和同意你 , 如果你沒有 , 你就記得在1968年的阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張很著名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	當時地球是從太空影像的第一次 , 它對我們宇宙的感知有著巨大的影響 , 而我們對地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼先拍了一幅相同的照片 , 沒有人類眼前看到的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的總結 , 從土星的另一邊看到的 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可思議的照片中 , 你會看到太陽的主要節奏 , 你會看到太陽的反射影像 , 而你看到這個節奏的形象 , 事實上 , 是由土衛二的爆發 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們就可以在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看我們自己的星球 , 被撞到土星的手臂 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些很深的移動 , 要從afar看待自己 , 捕捉我們的小小的藍色星球 , 在其他世界的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	這樣 , 我們的觀點是 , 可能在最後 , 最後 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到最好的獎勵 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到了2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人在災難後 , 愛滋病的消失後 , 隱藏了未知的土地和未知的道路 。 在這個短短的演講中 , 谷歌的麥加拉德•德薩德•德拉德的地圖製作者 , 一個團體在全球地圖上繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、科技、科技 , 合作 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	晚上 , 卡拉格達:製作地圖 , 來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 , 建立經濟體制 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , cycclonenaginagi摧毀了新奇的迷思 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要打破人民和供應區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有幫助到網路的受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖 , 很難相信2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地理細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國的頭部被標記為一個問題 , 世界上大部分的大面孔:沒有細節地圖 。
but help was coming .	但幫忙來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40名志工用一個新的軟體來繪製一萬二十萬公里的路徑 , 三千個醫院、邏輯和仰賴點 。
and it took them four days .	花了四天 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? 谷歌地圖學家 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖標記者是一種科技 , 使我們每個人能夠地圖地圖地圖地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從公路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 影片儲存到角落的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾•帕爾•帕爾•德羅德明白了 , 對於大部分開發中國家的經濟利潤的關鍵 , 是要擊敗大量未預算的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 一兆美金的真正產業在印度 , 只有一百萬美金 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 一百七十個國家有數百萬個使用者 , 創造了一幅細節的地圖 , 從來沒有想過 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	每處都有熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看一些使用者所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 人們在這個170個國家繪製世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑 , 只是在塞內加爾廣告道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更靠近家 , 查羅拉 , 一個n.g.g , 在孟加羅的路上 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何的結果 , 特徵辨識 , 機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一個電子編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們所未有的地球70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落在十個月的非暴力抗議中 , 阻止一個障礙 , 阻止他們在他們的橄欖球場 。 你聽到了嗎 ? 不認為 , 巴西的電影朱利亞•朱利亞•朱利亞 , 問我們為什麼我們只專注在以色列的衝突中暴力 , 而不是要讓非暴力的領袖帶給和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、娛樂、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞•巴基亞:專注注意非暴力的非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我已經把我的生活記錄下來 , 記錄以色列和巴勒斯和巴勒斯坦的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的意義來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 我花了數十個巴勒斯坦人 , 用非暴力的方式來保護他們的土地和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖忘記一個龐大的國家非暴力運動 , 終結職業 , 並在地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在這地面和感知之間的分歧 , 是為什麼我們還沒有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來談的是注意力、注意力的力量 , 以及在西岸的非暴力運動和發展 , 加薩和今天 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大部分的非暴力 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始非暴力 , 而是為了我們開始關注那些已有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個小村子 , 叫做budrus 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個分離障礙 , 其中一部分的障礙會被建造在村莊上 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被圍繞 , 所以他們會失去免費取得西岸的其他地方 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發當地的領導 , 他們推出了一個和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種情況 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的短片段 , 所以你有感知到它在地面上是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦婦女:我們被告知 , 從以色列中分離巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們了解牆壁會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:這句話的確 , 事實上 , 創造了一個解決方案來恐怖 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請到一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你有數十個以色列的兄弟和姊妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列的行動主義者:沒有比非暴力反對更害怕的軍隊 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推出士兵 , 但沒有人可以這樣做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為這些女孩可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔派派員:我們必須在傳統的思維中擁抱我們的思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬里•派派對:我們是完全的哈馬里 , 我們想要把它散播給所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	查理:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬和流行的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞報導:這句話持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列的邊界警察被送去分佈群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活躍的 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是泰國 。 每處槍擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列的積極主義者:我相信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊也有其他的 , 甚至還沒有編寫 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會停止 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	主持人:這是一個和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	查理:我們可以做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴拉:當我第一次聽到佛羅的故事 , 我驚訝的是 , 國際媒體已經無法覆蓋了七年前發生的非凡事件 , 在2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布德魯斯成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 經過了10個月的和平抗爭 , 說服了以色列政府 , 讓障礙離開土地和綠線 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦的領土 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	佛羅病毒的抗爭性從西岸傳播到村莊 , 到西方銀行和巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而 , 媒體大部分都留在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會帶來深刻的後果 , 對於非暴力的可能性 , 或甚至是在巴勒斯坦的生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗拒和非暴力抗拒 , 分享一個非常重要的事 ; 共同點 , 他們都是劇院尋求觀眾的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的演員是唯一一個人常被前面的封面 , 吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 對於非暴力領袖來說 , 很難讓公民歧視的社區變成一種可以在地址上的選擇 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能是 , 沒有意料到在房間的父母 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	為了讓孩子們越來越大的抗爭方式 , 就是給他注意他第一次丟下一台手指 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	螞蟻會變成童年心理學家所謂的功能行為 , 因為孩子已經學到 , 他能從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能激勵或不私人的行為 , 只因為給予予他們的孩子的注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但 , 對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可能受到影響 , 依據國際社群選擇專注注意力 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東的衝突的核心 , 把和平帶給和平的核心 , 要讓我們改變非暴力行為 , 藉由給予現今非暴力領袖的注意力 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在西岸、加薩和東耶路撒州的村莊裡 , 我看到了一部紀錄片的影響 , 即使一部紀錄片已經影響了轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做壁畫的村子裡 , 位於耶路撒冷 , 社區面臨了一個非常類似的突破 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有自由取得 , 不論是西岸銀行或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們花了大約兩年的時間都使用非暴力 , 但從沒有人注意到被關注 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們把最適當的和學會展示給日期 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯斯在電影中的故事 , 感受到 , 人們的確遵循他們所做的事 , 人們關心 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列的一面 , 有一個新的和平運動叫做義大利亞特 , 這意味著在希伯來的固定性 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者 , 被當作是他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告 , 以色列之前從來沒有活躍 , 看到電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華納和固態運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小型的獨立電影可以在改變非暴力行為的行為中扮演扮演角色 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大媒體玩家可能有能力 , 如果他們開始覆蓋週末非暴力的示範 , 例如bilin , nin , 華納 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰居 , 像sikharh , 沉默的非暴力領袖會變得更糟糕、更有價值、有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像他們從未發生過的那樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但 , 我第一次看到 , 如果我們這麼做 , 他們就會隨機拍攝 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多了 , 他們的影響力會在超過以色列人的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力是 , 終於能解開這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者證明了 , 非暴力在像布德魯這樣的地點 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意 , 讓他們可以證明它在各處運作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙斯基有一個很簡單但有啟發性的領導模式 , 都從一個黃金圈開始 , 問題是: 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德 , 以及威脅兄弟 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	布洛伊、商業、企業家、領導人、銷售、銷售、成功、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙斯汀克:領導人有多偉大的啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當我們假設時 , 事情不會發生 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或是更好的 , 你要如何解釋 , 其他人如何能夠達成所有假設的樣子 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 一年後 , 畢竟 , 他們比他們所有的競爭都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的能力 , 相同的職業 , 同一個顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為何他們看起來有點不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德引領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一在美國受苦的男人 , 他肯定不是那天唯一的偉大主持人 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何 , 威脅兄弟們能夠想出控制 , 權力飛行 , 當其他團隊有更好的資金 , 更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成男人飛行 , 摔角兄弟會打擊他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 , 它甚至深深地改變了我在運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大且鼓舞領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果或馬丁王或威脅的兄弟 , 他們都認為 , 行動和溝通的方式 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這對其他人來說完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是複製它 , 可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠啟發別人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不管你稱它為你不同的價值建議或你的正義過程或你的使用 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織都知道他們為何做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	「 為何 」 我不代表 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	結果是 , 結果總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	根據 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上你會出床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人會在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們認為 , 我們採取行動的方式 , 我們溝通的方式是來自外面的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最清楚的事物到難以置信 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但靈感的領袖和靈感組織 , 不論他們的大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都得到 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 用市場訊息可能聽起來就像這樣: 「 我們製造了很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮地設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一個嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷是這樣做 , 最多銷售的 , 那就是我們大多數人的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們怎麼做 , 我們說我們是不同的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們期待某種行為 , 一個投票 , 像這樣 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做事 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體 , 它有雷射海域 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果的溝通方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們做的一切 , 我們相信要挑戰現況 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思維 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓產品美麗的設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好才剛好製作了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同 ? 你準備好要從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是反轉資訊的秩序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	對我們來說 , 人們不買你做的事 ; 人們買你為何做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都很舒適 , 從蘋果買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒服地買蘋果的mp3球員 , 或蘋果的手機 , 或蘋果的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說的 , 蘋果只是電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何東西會從任何競爭者的競爭者中分散 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格來製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 蓋倫•艾爾在電視上出發 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格來製造平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	多年來 , 他們一直在製造平面螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	德萊爾和pda , 他們製作了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的產品 , 沒有人買了一顆 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像 , 買一個mp3的玩家 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為何你要從電腦公司買一個mp3的玩家 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和需要你所擁有的所有人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人商業 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	這是最好的部分:我告訴你們的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	生物學的十二氧化合物都被覆蓋在生物學上 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你仔細看人類大腦的交叉 , 從上角來看 , 你可以看到人類的大腦實際上被分成三種主要的元素 , 完全和黃金圓圈 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的同性腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新皮質 , 和 「 什麼 」 相對 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質對我們的理性和分析思考和語言是負責的 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間的兩個部分組成了我們的肢體大腦 , 我們的肢體大腦是對我們所有感受的負責 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	這對所有人的行為也是負責的 , 所有決策 , 也沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、利潤、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是沒有驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通時 , 我們就直接到大腦控制行為的一部分 , 然後我們允許人們用我們所說的 「 做 」 和 「 做 」 的 「 正確 」 來對待它 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策從這裡來的 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道嗎 , 有時候你可以給別人所有事實和人物 , 他們說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節說什麼 , 但這不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個版本 , 不是 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的部分 , 無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好的目標是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或有時候你會說你會帶著你的心臟 , 或是你帶著你的靈魂領袖 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭要打破它 , 那些不是其他的身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你肢體的大腦中 , 控制決策的部分 , 而不是語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為何你做你做的事 , 人們回應你為何要做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或更重要的是 , 成為你所做的事 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給你需要什麼的人 ; 目標是要賣給你相信你相信的人民 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不僅是僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是僱用你相信的人民 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你僱用人們 , 因為他們可以做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用你相信的人 , 他們會為你所相信的 , 他們會為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	另外一個例子是 , 這裡有一個比較好的例子 , 比有威脅兄弟更好 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelperpriley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀早期 , 權力飛行者的追求就像一天的點子一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelperponley , 我們假設 , 成為成功的回應 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即便現在 , 你問: 「 為什麼你的產品或你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的觀點 , 同樣的三件事:下降、錯誤的人、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是同樣的三件事情 , 讓我們來探究它 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelperponponley給了五萬美金 , 來找出這台飛行機 。
money was no problem .	金錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛大學工作 , 在密西西西斯頓工作 , 非常接觸 ; 他知道每天的所有大思維 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的腦袋 , 可以找到和市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他周圍 , 每個人都在追蹤拉伯利 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們怎麼來沒有聽過samuelpierponponley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠離俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾 , 威爾威爾•威爾 , 他們沒有我們所認為的成功 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們在他們的自行車店上付出他們的夢想 ; 沒有一個人在威脅兄弟的團隊有大學教育 , 甚至是ville或wilbur ; 紐約時報跟著他們在無所不在 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別是 , 奧ville和wilbur被引導 , 由一個目的 , 由一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出這台飛行機 , 它會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelperponngley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想成為富有的 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求豐富的追求中 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	再看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信威脅兄弟夢想的人 , 和他們一起合作 , 用血液、汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了付錢 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說故事 , 每次威脅兄弟出去 , 他們就得要花五組零件 , 因為在他們來到哪裡 , 他們就有多少次會撞擊 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 1903年 , 威脅兄弟飛行 , 沒有人會在那裡經歷它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現它 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步來說 , 拉利的證明是錯誤的:那天 , 威脅兄弟走了飛行 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個很棒的發現 , 傢伙 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不首先 , 他沒有富有 , 他不這麼有名 , 所以他辭掉了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引你相信的那些人很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做創新的法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你肯定知道這個詞 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們的第一個2%和1%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	下一個百分之十三十五的人口是早期的選手 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期 , 你的大多數人 , 你的主要和你的湖泊 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買到連接電話的唯一理由是 , 因為你再也不能再買羅字手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在不同的地方 , 在這個規模上 , 但創新的失敗法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大規模的成功或大規模的預算 , 直到你達到了15%和18%的市場拘留點 , 然後系統的限制 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你在新生意上有什麼轉換 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你們: 「 喔 , 這大概是10% 。 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試試超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有百分之十的 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就好像那顆腸子: 「 喔 , 他們就得到了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到你在做生意之前的結果 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	這裡是這一小塊你必須靠近的 , 如同傑夫•摩爾稱它為 「 跨越椅子 」 , 因為 , 早期的絕對不會嘗試某件事 , 直到其他人先試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期的選舉者 , 他們很舒適地做出這些決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們比較舒適 , 讓那些有直覺的決策 , 由他們對世界的相信而驅動的決定 , 不僅僅是產品能取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在線上六小時買iphone的時候 , 當他們第一次出門時 , 當你可以走進房間時 , 買了一支貨幣 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美元在平面螢幕上花了四萬美元的電視 , 儘管科技是郊區的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便說一提 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為科技很棒 ; 他們為自己做這件事 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 , 你做的就是證明你相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	一個人在前六個小時買iphone的原因是他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們想要看到的是什麼:他們是第一次 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗和有名的成功成功 , 讓創新的失敗 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 成功的回饋是金錢和右派人和權利市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從直到八、九年前 , 到目前為止 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手上沒有分散 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我每次都在我垃圾的時候投投入了dvr 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一種商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 他們的股票大約有30或40美金 , 然後放大了 , 卻從來沒有交易到10 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為 , 甚至在六歲以上交易 , 除了幾隻小小的骨頭 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為 , 當tivo發射了他們的產品 , 他們告訴我們他們所擁有的所有產品 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一產品 , 暫停了電視、技能商業、重新設計電視、記憶你的觀點 , 不用你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	歷史上大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 若你是那種喜歡控制你人生的每一個面向 , 男孩 , 我們就有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停住電視、技能商業化、記憶你的觀點習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 , 而你所做的就是為你所相信的證明 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在 , 讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的失敗法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 25萬人出現在華盛頓的大廳 , 聽見國王演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有邀請 , 沒有邀請 , 沒有網站來檢查約會 。
how do you do that ?	你該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的主管 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一在美國受苦的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些點子很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有去告訴美國需要改變的人們 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他走過來 , 告訴大家他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	那些相信他所相信的原因的人 , 他們會自自主 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人發聲 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	洛杉磯 , 有25萬人在正確的日子出現 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	其中有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己展現出來 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在公車上旅行八小時 , 才能站在華盛頓州的華盛頓區 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 不是黑色的白人:百分之25的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世界上有兩種法律:那些由較高權威所組成的人 , 那些是由男人所組成的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到人類所做出的所有法律 , 都與較高權威的法律相連 , 我們會生活在一個世界中 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好發生了 , 民權運動是最完美的幫助他帶來了他的原因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們遵循 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽政治人物現在 , 用他們非常複雜的12point計劃 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們不鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領袖 , 還有那些領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些引領我們激勵我們的人 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們遵守那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們遵守那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為何 」 開始的人有能力啟發他們周圍的人 , 或找到那些激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你該怎麼記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你在正確的方向移動 ? 神經科醫師 , 研究周圍的神經機制 , 以及他們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、知識、認知科學、認知科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neil燃燒:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡在哪裡 ?
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在一個大停車場時 , 我們要如何記得我們在哪裡停車 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這裡是問題在家裡 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	首先 , 我們會先從黃色顯示 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損害 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你就無法記住東西 , 包括你停車在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	以拉丁文為 「 海底 」 的名字 , 它是組合的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像其他的大腦 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一百億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元與彼此溝通 , 透過發送小小的脈搏 , 或訊號接觸到彼此 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體形成了兩個細胞 , 非常密集的連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們開始了解空間記憶如何運作 , 藉由從老鼠或老鼠身上記錄 , 或探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像一下 , 我們在這個老鼠的海馬體中錄下一個神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一個小小的電力時 , 就會有一個紅點和點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是 , 這個神經元知道每當老鼠在環境中被送到一個特定的地方 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會訊號傳給大腦的其他部分 , 透過發送一個小的電力刺激 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以展示神經元的比例 , 作為動物的地點的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物在其環境中的不同部分時 , 牠們會發出不同的神經元 , 例如在這個平方的盒子裡 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們共同組成了大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	地方細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監控電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了一個電玩遊戲 , 他們在小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	放置在海馬桶裡的細胞會被火 , 變成活躍的 , 每當他們穿過一個特定的地點時 , 就會發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個地方細胞怎麼知道 , 老鼠或人在其環境中在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線是很重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 最頂端的一個 , 像火火的牆壁之間 , 會在他們拉斯的牆壁之間 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴大這個盒子時 , 外面的位置會擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的一個位置 , 只要有一面牆 , 就會接近南方 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子內部 , 細胞會在兩個地方火 , 不管在南方有牆 , 都是動物在盒子內探索的 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這個預測 , 使你周遭的界限和方向的距離和方向 , 尤其是海馬體的重要性 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入中 , 細胞被發現到海馬體的哪一個計畫 , 它的反應是用來偵測界線 , 或邊緣 , 從老鼠或老鼠的探索 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以 , 左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每隻動物接近一面牆 , 或海岸 , 不管是邊緣或圓形盒的牆壁 , 甚至是桌子的邊緣 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發火 , 無論是南部的邊緣 , 不管是桌子或牆壁的邊緣 , 甚至是兩座桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	因此 , 我們認為 , 細胞會決定動物在哪裡去探索 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 像是這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記住的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常他們都很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 像我們和地方細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟是如何改變你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方的環境中 , 如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你把環境變得更大 , 他們認為旗幟是以相同的方式伸出去的 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就像你還記得 , 旗幟在哪裡儲存在你所有地方的細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以回溯到這個地點 , 這樣你最好的配合你所在的區域細胞的現狀模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	引導你回到你想記得的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在移動何處 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們採取一些外在路徑 , 或許我們停下來 , 我們就知道 , 因為我們的動作 , 我們能把這條路線整合起來 , 幾乎是頭部的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	放置細胞也得到這種條件 , 從一種叫做網格細胞的輸入 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞再次發現 , 在海馬體的輸入中 , 它們有點像地方細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠探索時 , 每個個體都在一整條不同的地點 , 在環境中 , 都在一個很驚人的三角形 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾張圖片中記錄下來 , 在不同的顏色中 , 每個顏色都有類似的圖案 , 每個細胞的圖形 , 就會轉換到其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的一顆火在這個圖上 , 綠色的那張 , 和這張照片上的藍色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 一起來 , 就好像老鼠可以把虛擬的地點放到它的環境中 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的拉丁和長期的線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的位置 , 讓它可以用自己的動作 , 知道它在環境中是什麼 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 由於所有圖案的圖案都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的圖案 , 以橘色的角度來看 , 意思是 , 大腦的所有網格活動應該改變我們是否在六個方向進行 , 或在六個方向進行進行 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放在磁共振儀裡 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 像我展示給你們看的 , 尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人體皮質上看到它 , 這是你在老鼠身上看到的磁鐵細胞的同一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記住他的車位在距離和方向的位置 , 要延伸建築物和圍繞在他停車的位置 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會被界限的細胞所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車公園中拿出來的路徑 , 它會被代表在網格細胞之中 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓地方細胞消防 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回溯到他移動的地點 , 以便發現 , 最好的組合圖案 , 正是他腦中的位置細胞 , 正是他停車車車的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	引導他回到那個地方 , 不尊重他的視覺特徵 , 像是他的車子是否在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被浪費了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 , 拿到它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這張圖案 , 我們在一系列的地點 , 每當我們做各種自動記憶任務時 , 例如 , 記住你上次婚禮 , 例如你在婚禮上去 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 或許是神經機制來代表我們周遭的空間 , 也用來產生視覺圖像 , 這樣我們就能重建空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想想像它們時發生的事件 。
